fyrste boke ¶the ſignification publyke weale called latyn reſpublica publike weale ſondry wiſe defined philoſophers knowing experience often repetition thyng graue ſadde importaunce wyll tedyous reders warke perchaunce parte haue ben trayned lerning conteynynge ſemblable matter haue compiled one definition many compendious fourme poore wytte deuyſe truſtynge thoſe fewe wordes true ſignification publike wele ſhall euidently appere reaſon ſatiſfie ¶a publike weale body lyuyng compact publike weale made ſōdry aſtates degree men whiche dyſpoſed order equytye gouerned rule moderation reaſon latin tongue called reſpublica whiche reſpublica worde re hath dyuers ſignifications dothe onely betoken called thynge whiche diſtinct perſon alſo ſignyfieth aſtate condityon ſubſtaunce profyt ¶in olde vulgare profytte called profytte weale called welthy countray wherin al thynge profitable welthy man ryche money ſubſtaunce publyke uarro ſayth publyke diriuied people latyn called populus wherfore ſemeth men haue ben longe abuſed calling rempublicam commune weale ſuppoſe ſo called euery thynge ſhoulde men commune without diſcrepaunce aſtate condition therto moued ſenſualite good reaſon inclination humanitie ſhall ſo one appere vnto wyll ſatyſfied eyther auctoritie naturall order example ¶fyrſte propre trewe ſignificatiō wordes publike comune whiche borowed latin tongue inſufficiencie owne langage ſhal ſufficiently declare blyndenes haue hitherto holden meynteyned ſayde opinion haue ſayde publyke toke begynnynge people whiche latin populus worde populus conteyned inhabytantes realme citie aſtate condition ſo euer ¶plebs engliſſhe called communaltie pleb whiche ſignifieth onely multytude wherin conteyned baſe vulgare inhabitantes auaunced honour dignitie whiche alſo vſed dayly comunication citie london city none alderman ſheriffes called communers countrey ſeſſions aſſembly gentyll men ſayinge none cō munaltye whiche proueth myne opinion pleb latine engliſhe communaltie plebeij communers plebeii ¶and conſequentely maye appere lyke diuerſitie engliſhe betwene publyke weale commune weale publyke commune ſhuld latyn betwene re publica re plebeia ſignification ſhulde commune weale eyther communers onely muſt welthy gentyl noble men nedy myſerable orelles excludyng gentylitie al men muſte one degre ſort newe name prouided moche pleb latine comminers englyſhe wordes onely made diſcrepance degree wherof procedeth ordre whiche ordre thynges well naturall ſupernaturall hath euer hadde ſuche preeminence therby incomprehenſible maieſtye god bryght leme torche candell declared blynd inhabitantes worlde ¶ ouer take awaye order thynges ſhulde remayne certes nothynge finally excepte ſomme man wolde imagine eftſones chaos whiche ſome expounded confuſe mixture chaos ¶ alſo lacke order nedes muſte perpetuall conflycte thynges ſubiecte nature thyng hym ſelfe onely maye nouryſſhed whan hath diſtroyed wherwith doth participate order creation hym ſelfe neceſſitie muſte peryſſhe wherof enſueth vniuerſall dyſſolution ¶ nowe proue example thoſe thynges within coumpaſſe mannes knowlege eſtimation ordre onely among men alſo god wyſedome bountye magnificence tonge pen ſufficiently expreſſed hath ſette degree aſtates glorious warkes ¶ fyrſte heuenly miniſters churche affyrmethe hath conſtituted dyuers degree called hierarch alſo chriſte ſayth euangeliſt houſe father whiche god many manſions ¶ treate whiche naturall elemenꝭ vnderſtandynge maye comprehended beholde foure elementes wherof body man compacte ſet theyr place called ſpheres higher lower accordynge ſouerayntie theyr nature ſaye fier moſte pure elemente hauinge nothyng corruptible place hygheſte aboue elementes ayer whiche next fyre moſt pure ſubſtance ſeconde ſphere place water whiche ſomewhat conſolidate approcheth corruptiō nexte vnto erthe erthe ſubſtance gros ponderous ſet elementes moſte loweſt ¶ beholde alſo order god hath put generally creature begynnynge mooſte inferiour baſe aſſendynge vpwarde made onely herbes garniſhe erthe alſo tree eminent ſtature herbes yet one degree quality ſome pleaſante beholde ſome delycate good taſte holſome medycinable ſome commodyous neceſſarie semblably byrdes beaſtis fyſſhes ſome good ſuſtināce man ſome beare thynges profytable ſondry vſes apte occupation laboure dyuerſe ſtrengthe fierſenes onely many ſtrengthe commoditie ſome ſerue pleſure none hath theſe quality fewe haue parte many ſpecially beautie ſtrengthe profytte founde hath many ſayde propreties ſette al eſtimation ordre place degree euidentely appereth euery kynde tree herbes birdes beaſtis fiſſhes beſide diuerſitie fourmes haue ſayth peculyer dyſpoſityon appropered vnto god theyr creatour ſo euery thynge ordre withoute ordre maye nothyng ſtable permanent maye called ordre excepte conteyne degree high baſe accordyng meryte eſtimation thynge ordered ¶ nowe returne aſtate manne kynde whoſe vſe ſayde creature ordeyned god alſo excelleth prerogatiue knowlege wyſedome ſemeth hym ſhulde leſſe prouidence god declared thā inferiour creature rather perfect ordre dyſpoſition therfore appereth god gyueth euery man like gyftes grace nature ſome ſome leſſe lyketh diuine maieſtie ne cōmune fantaſtical foles wolde haue thynges one man hath vertues good quality vuderſtā dynge ¶ ſtandynge moch vnderſtandynge moſte excellent gyfte man receyue creation wherby doth approche moſte nyghe vnto ſimilitude god whiche vnderſtandynge pryncipall parte ſoule therfore congruent accordynge one excelleth influence therby beinge nexte ſimilitude maker ſo ſhulde aſtate perſon auaunced degree place vnderſtandynge maye profyt alſo dyſtrybuted ſondry vſes faculty office neceſſary lyuynge gouernaunce mankynd lyke angel whiche moſt feruent contemplation hygheſt exalted glorye opinion holy doctours alſo fire moſt pure elementes alſo dothe clarifie inferioure elemētes deputed higheſt ſphere place worlde whiche excelle influence vnderſtan dynge imploye deteynyng within boundes reaſon ſhewe howe prouide theyr neceſſarie lyuynge ſuche ought ſette highe place reſidue maye ſe alſo ſene beames theyr excellente wytte ſhewed throughe glaſſe auctoritie inferiour vnderſtanding maye directed way vertu cōmodious liuing ¶ vnto men ſuche vertue verye equitie apperteineth honour theyr iuſt honour rewarde duetie men labour muſte alſo meynteyned accordynge theyr merytes moche ſayde perſons excellinge knowlege wherby gouerned mynyſters profite cōmoditie whiche haue equall vnderſtandynge whiche exerciſe artificiall ſcience corporall labour trauaile theyr ſuperiours alſo owne neceſſitie houſeband man fedethe hym ſelfe clothe maker clothe maker apparayleth ſelf houſebande bothe ſocour artificer artificer artificer gouernours ¶ gouernours ſayde nothyng acquire ſayd influence knowlege theyr owne neceſſities imploye power theyr wyttes theyr dylygence preſeruation inferiours amonge whiche inferiours alſo behoueth diſpoſition order accordyng reaſon ſay ſlouthfull idell perſon participate hym induſtrious taketh peyne wher fruites labour ſhulde diminiſſhed wherin ſhulde none equalite therof ſhulde procede dyſcourage finally dyſolution lacke prouyſion wherfore none wiſe ſtand reaſon aſtate perſon preeminence lyuynge ſhuld eſtemed vnderſtandynge labour policie vnto muſte added augmentation honour ſubſtaunce whiche nat impreſſeth reuerence wherof procedeth due obedience amonge ſubiectes alſo inflameth men naturally inclined idelnes ſenſual appetite coueyte lyke fortune cauſe diſ poſe ſtudy occupation ¶ howe conclude fyrſte aſſertion argument al thing comune lacketh ordre ordre lackethe thynge odyouſe vncomly haue dayly experience pannes pottes garnyſſhe well ketchyn yet ſhuld chā bre none ornamente alſo beddes teſtars pyllowes beſeme hall carpettes kuſſhines become ſtable semblably potter tynker onely perfecte theyr crafte ſhal littell miniſtration iuſtice ploughman carter ſhall make foble anſwere ambaſſadour alſo wayuer fuller ſhuld vnmete capitaine army office gouernour wherfore conclude publyke weale lyke god hath dyſpoſed ſayde influence vnderſtandynge alſo appoynted degree place accordynge excellencie therof therto alſo wolde ſubſtance conuenient neceſſarie ornamente ſame alſo impreſſeth reuerence due obedience vulgare people cōmunaltie without ſayde publike weale may affyrmed houſe without propre neceſſary ornamentes well ſufficiently furnyſhed one ſoueraygne gouernour ought publyke weale damage hath happened wher multytude hath hadde equall auctorite without ſoueraygne cap ii lyke caſtel fortres ſuffiſeth one owner ſoueraign mo like power authorite ſeldome cometh warke perfection beynge redy made one diligently ouerſeth neglecteth conten tion ſubuerted cōmeth ruyne ſēblable wiſe doth publike weale hath chiefe gouernours one example may take grekes amonge diuers city weare diuers fourmes publyke weales gouerned multitude wherin one moſte tollerable gouernance rule alway permitted excelled vertue greke tonge called ariſtocratia latin optimorum potentia engliſhe rule mē beſt diſpoſition chebanes lōg time obſerued ¶ publyque weale amonge athenienſis equalytye aſtate among people hole conſente theyr citie dominion gouerned whiche moughte well called monſter many heedes neuer certayne ſtable often tymes baniſſhed ſlewe beſt cytezins whiche theyr vertue wyſe dome moſte profited publyke weale maner gouernaunce called greke dimocratia latin popularis dimocratia potentia englyſſhe rule comminaltie theſe two gouernances none may ſufficient firſt whiche conſiſteth good men vertue ſo conſtant multitude ſome beynge one authoritie incenſed glorie ſome ambition couetiſe deſyre treaſure poſſeſſions wherby falle contention fynally achiueth ſuperioritie hole gouernāce reduced vnto fewe nombre whiche fearynge multitude theyr mutabilitie intent kepe drede rebell ruleth terrour crueltie thynkynge therby kepe ſelfe ſuertie withſtandynge rancour coarcted longe deteyned narowe roume laſt braſteth intollerable vyolence bryngeth confuſion power practized hurte many continue ¶the popular aſtate thyng vary equalitie ſubſtāce eſtimation multitude people haue ouer moch libertie neceſſitie one theſe inconueniēces muſt happen either tyranny moch fauor wold eleuate ſuffre none equalitie elles rage communaltie whiche al rule mooſte feared lyke commune fele ſome ſeueritie doo humbly ſerue obeye ſo imbracing lycence refuſe brydeled flyng plunge one throwe downe theyr gouernour order euery thyng without iuſtice vengeāce ¶grammer beinge introduction vnderſtandynge autors made long exquiſite lerner maner mortifyeth courage tyme cometh moſt ſwete pleſante redynge olde auctors ſparkes ſeruente deſyre lernynge extyncte interlaſynge therwith wolde redde chylde eſopes fable greke whiche argument child moch eſopes fable delyte ſurely moche pleaſante leſſon alſo profitable well elegante brefe ſtandyng hath moch varietie wordes therwith moche helpeth vnderſtandynge greke alſo thoſe fable included moche morall polytyke wyſedome wherfore teachynge maiſter dilygently muſte gather gether thoſe fable whiche maye moſt accommodate aduauncement ſome vertue wherto perceyueth chylde inclyned rebuke ſomme vyce wherto fyndeth nature dyſpoſed therin maiſter oughte exercyſe wytte well make child plainly vnderſtand fable alſo declaring ſignification therof compendiouſly purpoſe fore ſene allwaye well leſſon auctors chylde ſhall lerne eyther greke latine verſe proſe perfectly without boke wherby ſhal onely atteyne ¶notwithſtandyng moche ſayd warkes longe require therfore great tyme lerned kanned ſome latin auctour wolde therwith myxt ſpecially uirgile whiche warke called eneidos moſte lyke uirgilius homere almoſte ſame homere latin alſo ioining together thoſe auctors one ſhall better vnderſtande veryly ſayd one auctour ſerueth ſo dyuers wittes doth uirgile affect deſire wherto childes fantaſy dyſpoſed ſome uirgils warkes may foūden matter therto apt propiſe thing famyliar bucolikes warke ſoo nyghe approcheth cōmune dalyance maners chyldrē praty cōtrouerſies ſimple ſhepeherdes therin conteyned wonderfully reioyceth chylde hereth wel declared knowe mine owne experience georgikes lorde pleaſaunt varietie dyuers graynes herbes flowres deſcribed redynge therin ſemeth man delectable gardeyne paradyſe ploughe manne knoweth ſo moch houſebandry expreſſed delytynge good horſys ſhall therto enflamed redynge bredyng cheſyng kepyng declaration wherof uirgille leaueth farre behynde hym breders hakney menne ſkorſers aſtronomer exactely ſetteth ordre courſe celeſtiall bodyes truely doth deuine pronoſtications tymes yere quality future aſtate thynges prouided huſebandry thā uirgile doth recite warke chylde haue delyte huntynge pleaſure ſhall take fable ariſteus ſemblably hunting dido eneas whiche diſcryued mooſte elegantly boke eneidos haue pleaſure wraſtling renning lyke exerciſe ſhall ſe pleſaunte eſbatementes whiche doone eurealus troyans whiche accompanyed eneas take ſolace herynge mynſtrelles mynſtrel may compared iopas whiche ſange dido eneas blinde demodocus played ſange moſte ſwetely dyner kynge alcinous made uliſſes whoſe dityes melody excelled farre ſonges minſtrelles homere uirgile excell poetes ¶ deſyrous mooſte parte child thinges maruailous exquiſite hath viſa ge ſome thinges incredyble wherat ſhal wonder whan ſhal beholde eneas folowe sibille hel ſhal drede terrible vyſages cerberus gorgon megera fury monſters howe ſhall abhorre tyranny fraude auarice whan nedefull aſſailynge enemyes finally haue ſayde noble uirgile like good noriſe giueth child wyll take euery thynge apte witte capacitie wherfore ordre lerninge preferred autor latine ¶ wolde ſet nexte vnto hym two bokes ouid one called metamorphoſios whiche moche ſaye changynge men fygure fourme intytled de faſtis ceremony gentyles ſpecyally romaynes expreſſed bothe ryght neceſſarye vnderſtandynge loſte whiche mought better employed ſuche autors minyſter eloquence ciuile polycie exhortation vertue ¶ wherfore place lette v brynge horace conteyned moch varietie lerning quickeneſſe ſentence poet may enterlaced leſſon odiſſea homere wherin declared wonderfull prudence fortitude uliſſes paſſage troye chylde induced make verſis imytation uirgile homere ſhulde myniſter hym moche dylectation poetis neceſſary chyldehode gentyll manne moche theſe doubt wyll ſuffyce vntyll paſſe age xiii yeres whiche tyme childhode declyneth reaſon waxeth rype apprehendeth thinges cō ſtante iugement ¶ wolde haue remembred require al theſe warkes throughly red chylde time almoſte impoſſible doſyre haue euery ſayde bokes ſoo moch inſtruction may take therby ſome profytte chyldes courage poetis de fēded pryſed infiamed frequente redynge noble poetes dayely deſyreth haue experyence thoſe thynges ſo vehemently commende write ¶ leonidas noble kynge spartanes beynge one demaunded eſtimatiō poetry tirtaeus ſuppoſed written anſwering ſayd ſteryng mindes yong men excellent moche beinge meued verſys renne batayle regardynge peryll men inflamed martiall courage ¶ whan man comen rype yeres reaſon hym confyrmed ſerious lernyng long experience ſhall redyng tragedy execrate abhorre intollerable life tirātes ſhall contemne foly dotage expreſſed poetes laſciuious ¶ wyll leaue ſpeake firſte parte concerning leſſon oratours euery wōderful profitable hauinge almoſt many wyſe ſentences hath wordes ſo ſwete delectable rede hym almoſt ſeme vnſauery tedyous perſuadynge well prynce pryuate perſon cooke ſeruice wyll fyrſte examine diligently howe many ſortes meates potage ſauces perfectely make howe well ſeaſon maye pleaſant nouriſhynge yea fauconer wyll ſcrupuluſly enquire ſkyll hath fedynge inſtructed vertue whoſe lyfe ſhall princypall monument name honour neuer maketh enquirie may haue ſchole maiſter howe lytel charge one perchance foū den well lerned whiche wyll take peines teache almoſt euery poete fetched moſt ſubtile parte naturall queſtions theſe well nyghe wordes quintilian beholde fewe grammariens deſcription realme ¶ undoutedly realme many wel lerned name ſchole mayſter ſoo moche hadde contempte alſo theyr labour abundante ſalaries moughte requited ryghte ſufficiente able induce theyr herers excellente lernynge ſo plucked away grene er doctrine ſufficiently rooted hath gyuen perſonage courage apte warres alſo gentylwomen feare neyther ſonne wynde appayringe theyr beautie perauenture ſhall laſſe idell ſhulde home theyr chambres ¶ kylling dere bowes greyhoū de haukinge remembrance vſed auncient tyme amonge noble pryncis call auncyente tyme thouſand yeres paſſed ſens whiche tyme vertue nobleneſſe hath rather decayed increaſed coulde neuer knowe founde fyrſt dyſporte ¶ plinius maketh menciō viii boke hyſtorye nature partes grece called thracia menne haukes confederacie toke byrdes gether wyſe menne ſprange byrdes buſihes haukes ſorynge ouer beate downe ſoo men moughte eaſyly take dyd men departe equally praye faukons beynge well ſerued eftſoones cuſtome repayred ſuche place beinge lofte perceyued men purpoſe aſſembled ¶ whiche reherſal plinius may coniecte thratia came diſporte haukynge doubt many well haue ſene ſemblable experience wilde hobies whiche ſome countreys champaine ſore lie lofte houeringe ouer larkes quayles kepe downe ground while awayte praye take wyſe ſo euer beginninge haukynge ſurely ryghte delectable ſolace thoughe therof commeth ſo moch vtilitie concernynge exerciſe doth huntynge wolde oure faukons moughte ſatisfied dyuyſion pray faukons tracia nedeed deuour hennes realme ſuche nombre vnles ſhortely conſidered faukons broughte homely dyete ryght lykely within ſhorte ſpace yeres familiar pultrie ſhalbe ſcarce nowe partriche feſaunt ſpeake diſprayſe faukons whiche kepeth lyke cokneyes meane gentyl men honeſte houſeholders whiche care gentyl enterteinement frendes find dyſhe ſaye trouthe noble men ſhal ryght ſhortly eſpie whan come ſodeinly theyr frendes houſe vnpurueied lacke longe warnynge ¶ returne purpoſe undoubtedly haukynge meaſurably vſed paſſetyme gyueth man good appetite ſupper leaſt waye withdraweth hym daliaunce diſportes diſhoneſt body ſoule perchaunce pernicious ¶ nowe purpoſe declare ſome thing concernynge daunſynge wherin merite prayſe dyſprayſe ſhall expreſſe ſuche fourme truſt reder ſhal fynde therin rare ſynguler pleaſure alſo good lernynge thinges yet communely knowen vulgare red hym hath good opportunitie quyete ſylence doubte ſhall take therby ſuche commoditie loked haue founden exerciſe whiche parte ſad men ſo lyttell eſtemed daunſynge reproued capitulo xix opinion daunſing generally repugnaunt vnto vertue thoughe ſome perſones excellently lerned ſpecially diuines ſo affirme whiche alwaye haue theyr mouthes whan come pulpette ſayinge noble doctour ſainct auguſtine better delue go ploughe ſondaye thanne daunce whiche moughte ſpoken kynde daunſynge vſed tyme ſainct auguſtine whan euery thing empire rome declined perfection olde maner danſynge forgoten none remayned laſciuious corrupted myndes daunſed prouoked ſynne ſemblably ſome daye alſo tyme idolatry nat clerely extinct diuers fragmentes therof remayned euery region perchance ſolemne daū ſes whiche celebrate vnto paynim falſe goddis yet continued aſmoch pure religion chriſt nat al place conſolidate paſtors curate dyd winke ſuche recreatiōs fearynge ſhulde haſtily haue remeued induced ſodaynly ſeueritie goddis lawes ſhulde ſtyre people therby generall ſedition imminent daunger ſubuertion chriſtis hole religion late ſowen among nat yet ſufficiently rooted wyſe diſcrete doctour ſaynte auguſtine vſynge art oratour wherin right excellent omytting rigorous menace terrour diſſuaded theym moſte eaſieſt way maner ceremony belō gyng idolatrie preferryng bodyly occupation therby aggrauatynge offence god ceremony ſens occupation whiche neceſſarye man ſuſtinaunce due tymes vertuous nat withſtandynge prohibited vſed ſondayes yet theſe wordes noble doctour ſo generall diſprayſe daunſynge ſome men ſuppoſe two cauſes fyrſt compariſon preferreth nat daunſynge ioyneth therto vycious exercyſe annecteth tyllyng diggynge erthe whiche labour incident man lyuyng cō teyned nothynge vycyous wherefore preemynence therof aboue daunſynge qualifyeng offence beinge done due tyme ſaye holy daye concludeth nat daunſynge tymes euery maner vnlaufull vicious conſyderynge certayn caſes exſtreme neceſſytie menne mought bothe ploughe delue without god offence alſo ſhall ſeme ſeriouſly examyne ſaid wordes therein sayncte auguſtine dothe nat prohybyte daunſynge ſo generally taken onely ſuche daunſes whiche late ſayde ſuperſtytious conteyned theym ſpyce ydolatrie elles dydde vncleane motion countynances irritate myndes dauncers venereall luſtes wherby fornicatiō auoutry dayly increaſed alſo thoſe daūces enterlaſed dities wan ton loue rybaudry frequente remembraūce moſt vile idolles uenus baccus daunce honour memory whiche moſte abhorred chriſtis religion ſauering auncient errour paganiſme ¶ wold god thoſe name day vſed balades ditty courtes pryncys noble men many good wittes corrupted ſemblable fantaſies whiche better wyſe employed moughte haue bene neceſſary publyke weale theyr prince honour nowe wyll leaue ſeryouſe matter diuines perſwade dyſſuade herein accordynge theyr offyces ſens myne opinion ſayncte auguſtine bleſſed clerke reproueth ſo generally daunſynge maye laufully reherſe ſome kynde therof maye neceſſary alſo commendable takynge exerciſe ſhal nowe procede ſpeake fyrſt beginnyng therof great eſtimation dyuers region fyrſt beginning daunſinge olde eſtimation therof cap xx ſendry opinion oryginall beginninge daunſynge poetes faine whan saturne whiche deuoured dyuers child ſemblably wolde haue done iupiter bhea mother iupiter deuiſed curetes whiche mē armes countrey ſhuld daunſe armour playing curetes theyr ſwordes ſheldes ſuche fourme newe pleaſaunt deuiſe ſhulde aſſuage melancolye saturne meane tyme iupyter cōueyed phrigia saturne alſo purſuyng hym bhea ſemblably taught peple called coribantes cāce nother fourme saturne choribā te eftſones demulced appaiſed whiche fable hath reſemblaunce hiſtory bible fyrſte boke kinges remēbred saul whō god chaſe keper aſſes kynge iewes ſtature excelled aboue men heed declinyng lawes preceptes god poſſeſſed iuell ſpirite often time turmented vexed hym remedye founde none dauid whiche hym kynge tyme propre childe playinge ſwetely harpe pleaſaunt perfect harmonie reduced mynde priſtinate eſtate durynge tyme played ſpirite ceſſed vexe hym whiche ſuppoſe hapned nat onely efficacie muſyke albeit therin moche power well repreſſynge excytinge naturall affectes alſo vertue ingenerate chylde dauyd playd god alſo p̄deſtinate great kyng great prophete ſouerayn gyftes grace nature endowed myghty god ſaid founde man harte pleaſure nowe retourne ſpeake daunſynge ¶ interpretours poetes imagin proteus proteus ſuppoſed haue turned ſelf ſondry figure ſom tyme ſhew hym ſelfe like ſerpent ſome tyme lyke lyon otherwhyles lyke water tyme like flame fyre ſignifieth none delyuer crafty daunſer whiche daunſe coulde imagyne inflexion ſerpent ſoft delectable flowynge water ſwiftnes mountynge fyre fierſe rage lyon violence furye lybarde whiche expoſition nat diſpraiſed ſins diſcordeth nat reſon one opinyon whiche wylle reherſe merye fantaſy therin cōteined faythe credite gyuen therto ¶ ouer syracuſis greate auncient citie sicile raigned cruel tyrant gelo kynge sicile called gelo horryble tyranny oppreſſions brought hym ſelfe hatrede people whyche perceyuynge leſte mutuall communication ſhulde conſpyre agaynſt hym rebellyon prohibited men vnder terrible menace man woman ſhulde ſpeake vnto nother ſtede wordes ſhoulde vſe neceſſary affayres countenaunces token mouynges theyr fete handes eien whiche neceſſitie fyrſte vſed laſte grewe perfecte delectable daunſynge gelo nat withſtandynge folyſhe curioſite laſte ſlayne people moſte myſerably although hyſtorie true yet nat daunſynge tyme fyrſt begon orpheus muſeus moſte auncient poetes alſo homere whiche longe afore gelo make mention daūſing delvs whiche moſte ancient temple apollo ſolemnitie done without daunſynge ¶ alſo indie people honoreth ſonne aſſemble togyther whanne ſonne fyrſte appereth ioyned daunce ſalute hym ſuppoſinge moche mouethe without ſenſible noyſe pleaſeth beſt like wyſe ſaluted ſay pleaſante motion ſilence ¶ interpretours plato thinke wonderful incōprehenſible ordre che daunſynge wherfore nere approched temperaunce ſubtyle modulation ſayd ſuperiour bodyes perfect commēdable theyr daunſynge whiche mooſte lyke trouthe opinion haue hitherto founden ¶ fable omytte preſente tyme nowe wyll expreſſe eſtymation daunſyng hadde aunciente tyme alſo ſondry fourmes daunſynge ſuch hadde ſemblaunce vertue kunnynge ¶ whan arke god wherin put archa federis table commaundementes yerde wherwith moiſes deuided red ſee miracle preſence pharao kynge egipte alſo parte manna wherwith chyldren iſrael fedde fourty yeres deſert recouered philiſties brought vnto citie gaba holy kyng dauid kyng dauid daunſing opēty wearynge hym linen ſurpleſſe daunſed ſayd arke folowynge hym gret nombre inſtrumētis muſike wher wyfe micol daughter kynge saul diſdayned ſcorned hym wherwith holy ſcripture ſaythe myghty god moche diſpleaſed dauid ceſſinge daunſed ioyouſely citie maner honourynge ſolemne feaſte whiche amonge iewes one chiefe principall wherwith god pleaſed obſeruances done vnto hym time ¶ wyll trouble reders innumerable ceremonyes gentyles comprehended daunſinges ſens oughte noumbred amonge ſuperſtytions wyll declare howe wyſe menne valiaunte capitaynes imbraced daunſyng ſoueraygne profytable exerciſe ¶ licurgus gaue firſte lawes lacedemones people grece ordeyned child ſhuld taught diligētly daūſe armure fight tyme warres ſhoulde meue bataile againe enemy fourme maner daunſynge ¶ semblably old inhabitātes ethiopia ioynyng theyr batayles whan trumpettes inſtrumentes ſoune daūce ſtede quiuer haue theyr dartes ſet theyr heades lyke rayes beames ſonne wherwith beleue put theyr enemy feare ¶ alſo lefull caſte darte enemie daunſyng onely rude people eſtemed ſo moche daunſynge alſo moſte noble grekes whiche theyr excellencie proweſſe wiſedome called half goddis achilles ſonne pirrhus diuers wherfore homere among highe benefites god giueth man reciteth daunſynge ſaythe fyrſte boke iliados god graunteth ſome man proweſſe martiall nother daunſinge ſong harmonical ¶ suppoſe ye romaynes grauitie maners paſſed greekes gret pleaſure daunſing romulus fyrſt kyng romaine builder citie rome ordeyne certain prieſtes miniſters god mar vnto tyme chriſtned noble men princis childrē vſing moch diligence ſuite coueyted college ſayde daunſers ¶ ouer emperours moſt noble delited daunſyng perceiuing therin perfecte meaſure may called modulation wherin ſome daunſers olde tyme ſo wonderfully excelled wolde playnely expreſſe daunſynge without wordes dyttie hiſtories hole circumſtaunce affaire conteyned wherof ſhal reherſe two maruailouſe experience ¶ rome tyme nero philoſopher called demetrius whiche ſecte moche abandoned ſhame faſtenes theyr wordes actes called cinici engliſhe doggyſhe demetrius often reprouinge daunſynge wolde ſaye nothynge therin importaunce none counterfaytyng feete handes armonye ſhewed rebecke ſhalme inſtrument motyons vayne ſeperate vnderſtandyng purpoſe efficacie wherof herynge famouſe daunſer one ſemed without good lernynge remembraunce many hiſtories came demetrius ſayde vnto hym syre humbly deſire refuſe honeſtie preſence beholdyng daunce whiche ye ſhall ſe without ſoune inſtrument ſhall ſeme worthy diſprayſe vtterly banyſhe confounde ſcience whervnto demetrius graunted yong man daūſed aduoutry mar uenus therin expreſſed howe uulcane housbande uenus therof beinge aduertyſed ſonne whiche dyd ſo ſubtile crafty geſture ſuche playne declaration euery acte mater whiche thynge mooſte dyfficyle ſuche grace beautie alſo wytte ſo wonderfull pleaſaunte demetrius ſemed therat reioyſyng delytynge cried loude voyce man onely ſe alſo thou doeſt ſemeth alſo thy handes thou ſpekeſte whiche ſayinge confirmed al tyme preſent ¶ ſame yonge man ſonge daunſed tyme emperour nero whan alſo whan hadde taken leaue emperour departe emperour offered gyue hym thynge thoughte moughte commoditie ye maye ſayde kynge bounteouſelye rewarde ye lende yonge man daunſed maieſtie nero wondring requiring ſo importunately deſyred daū ſer cōmoditie daunſer mought vnto hym syr ſadie kynge haue dyuers confins neyghbours ſondry langages maners wherfore haue often tymes nede many interpretours wherfore hadde man ſhulde haue thynge neyghbours wolde ſo faciō geſture expreſſe euery thing teche ſame henſforth ſhulde haue nede interpretour ¶ alſo auncient philoſophers commended daunſynge ſo facionynge body ¶ cōſidered ſayd anciente tyme dyuers maners daunſyng varied name lyke wyſe dydde tune inſtrumente ſemblably haue daye thoſe name ſome general ſome ſpeciall general name giuen mā wold vehemēt woman delycate leſſe aduanſynge body ſignifienge courage ſtrength ought mā pleſant ſobreneſſe ſhuld woman wſſe fierſenes ioyned myldeneſſe makethe seueritie hardyneſſe timeroſitie importaunce ¶ nowe bycauſe paſſe tyme cōpared wherin may founden recreation meditation vertue haue among honeſt paſtymes wherin exerciſe body noted daunſyng excellent vtilitie comprehēding fled eſchewed named ariſtotel mother vertues philoſophers called capytayne mayſtres vertues ſome houſe wyfe moche diligēce ſhe doth inueſtigate prepare place apt cōuenient vertues ſhall execute theyr power office wherfore salomon ſaith lyke water ſhewed vyſages beholde prov 27 ſo vnto menne prudent ſecretes men harte openly diſcouered vertue beinge ſo cōmodious man porche noble palayce inſtructiō ſurely grauē table remembrance wherfore haue courage ſtered towarde honour perfecte nobilitie let approche paſſe tyme either ſelfes prepare daunſe el leſte way beholde watchynge eyen daunſe truely kepyng iuſt meaſure tyme vnderſtanding inſtruction muſt marke well ſondry motion meaſures true form daunſinge ſpecially obſerued ¶ firſt meuing euery daunſe called honour reuerent inclinatiō curteſie lōge deliberatiō pauſe one motion comprehending tyme thre motion ſetting forth foote may ſignified begynning actes ſhulde due honour god whiche roote prudence whiche honour compact theſe thre thinges feare loue reuerēce begynnynge al thinges ſhoulde aduyſedly ſome tracte tyme beholde foreſee ſucceſſe enterpryſe ¶ ſeconde motion two nombre may ſignified celerite ſlowneſſe celeritie quiknes ſlownes whiche two ſeme diſcorde effectes natural propreties therfore maye welle reſembled braule daunſynge braule englyſhe tonge ſay men braule whan betwene altercation wordis yet two ſpringeth excellent vertue wherevnto lacke name englyſhe wherfore cōſtrained vſurpe latin worde callynge maturitie whiche worde though ſtrange darke yet declaryng vertue mo wordes name iugement ouercomen poore man laate infraunchyſed therfore thou mayſte nothynge doo lyghtlyer plede ageynſt emperour say nowe alone let thy purpoſe ſuppoſiſt thou paule fabius maximus coſſes seruiliis aunciente houſes rome ſuche ſorte noble men nat whiche haue vayne glorious name ſuche merites adorned propre image wyll ſuffre finally ſaid emperor talked hym ſpace two howres gyue thy lyfe cinna gaue emperour al goodes poſſeſſions neuer auguſtus daunger treaſone ¶ ſufficient prayſe may giuen moſte noble prudente emperoure chambre aloone without men ordenance weapon perchaunce without harnes haſtily puniſſheth oft tymes ſone repenteth ouer moch correcteth obſerueth none equitie ye aſke mercye temperaunce mynde hym hath power auenged called latine clementia alway ioyned reaſon euery lyttel occaſion meued compaſſion beholdynge man punyſſhed condygnely offence lamenteth waylethe called pitiouſe ſyckeneſſe mynde wherewith daye parte menne diſeaſed yet ſikenes moch war adding one word liberalitie ¶ ariſtotle defineth liberal man whiche liberal man ethic 2 doth erogate accordinge rate ſubſtance oportunitie hapneth ſayth alſo ſame place liberalytie multitude quātite gyuen habite facion gyuer gyueth accordynge habilitie neither tulli approueth liberalitie wherin myxture auarice rapine properly liberalitie exacte iniuſtely violence crafte take goodes frō particuler per ſons diſtribute multitude take frō many iniuſtly enriche therwith perſonne fewe ſame autour ſayth laſt precept concernynge benefytes rewardes take good hede contende agaynſt equitie ne vpholde none iniurie ¶ nowe wyll procede ſeriouſly due forme ſpeke pticulerly theſe thre vertues withſtanding ſuche affinitie betwene beneficence liberalitie beinge alwayes vertue tende one cōcluſion purpoſe ſay uertue meane determined reaſon meane myddes two thinges vycious one ſurpluſage lacke nedes muſt beneficence liberalitie • apitall vertues magnificence procedeth frō approching extreme partes may turned vyce lacke brydell reaſon beneficence meanes vicious beneficēce retayne ſtyl name semblably liberalitie ariſtotle ſaith meſure liberalite welle gyuynge takynge money goodes onely lyberall whiche diſtributeth accordynge conſiderations iu gyuynge ſubſtance expedient ther fore ought cōſider ſhuld gyue howe moche whan lyberalitie taketh name ſubſtance perſone whome procedeth reſteth nat quātitie qualite thin ge gyuen naturall diſpoſition gyuer ¶ greate alexander tyme vanquyſhed darius battayle one alexand ſouldiours broughte vnto hym heed ennemy ſlayne whiche kynge thankefully ſwete countenance receyued takyng cuppe golde fylled good wyne ſayde vnto ſowldyour olde tyme cuppe golde rewarde ſuch vertue thou haſte ſhewed whyche ſemblablye thou ſhalt receyue whan ſouldior ſhamefaſtnes refuſed cup alexāder added vnto theſe wordes cuſtome gyue cuppe emptie alexander gyueth fulle wyne good handſell ¶ wherwith expreſſed lyberal hart moche comforted ſouldiour gyuen hym great citie ¶ ouer lyberalle neglecteth nat ſubſtance goodes ne giueth liberal men vſeth ſo may contynually helpe therwith gyueth whan whome oughte employed therfore may ſaide vſeth euery thynge beſte exercyſeth vertue whiche thyng moſt appropried rycheſſe nombre thynges maye eyther good yuell whyche arbytremente gyuer cauſe lyberalitie benefycence ſuche affinitie one maye neuer ſeperate employment moneye nat lyberalitie nat good ende purpoſe ¶ noble emperours antonine alexander seuerus gaue reuenues antonyne liberal alexander emperor empire inumerable ſubſtāce reedifieng city cōmune houſes decaied age erth quaues ſubvted wherin practiſed liberalite alſo beneficēce ¶ tyberius nero caligula heliogabalus ſemblable monſters whiche prodigalite exhauſted conſumed infinite treaſures bordell houſes place abomination vſed alſo enryching ſlaues concubynes baudes nat named lyberall ſuffren therfore perpetual reproche writars beinge called deuourers waſters treaſure wherfore moch lyberalitie holly reſteth gyuynge money ſomtyme coloureth vyce beneficence neuer taken better parte tullie ſaith taken vertue liberalitie cōmeth coffer ¶ alſo man diſtributeth ſubſtance many perſons laſſe liberalitie ſhal vſe ſo bounteouſnes bountie minyſhed onely called beneficiall vſe vertue beneficence whiche conſiſteth coū ſaylynge helpynge aſſiſtence tyme nede ſhall alwaye fynde coadiutours ſupportours gentyll courage douteles maner gen tylnes conſiſteth labour ſtudie diligēce cōmendable extēdeth alſo may profite perſons whiche reſteth rewardes expences retourne liberalitie ¶ greater foly may thā thing prodigalitie man moſt gladly dothe endeuour hym ſtudye maye longer done wherfore tulli calleth prodigalle inordynate feaſtes bankettes vayne playes huntynges doo ſpende theyr ſubſtance thoſe thinges wherof ſhall leaue ſhort remembrance wherfore reſort counſaylle aryſtotle expreſſed lyberalytie noble manne ſpecyally commended though ſomewhat excede termes meaſure yf well duely employed acquireth perpetualle honour gyuer moche frute ſyngular commoditie therby encreaſeth honeſte vertuous perſonages aduaunced wel rewarded ſtereth courage menne whyche haue ſparke vertue encreaſe therin theyr force endeuoure wherefore nexte helpynge relieuyng communaltie great parte lyberalitie employed men vertue good quality wherin required good election iuge ment hope rewarde fauour vnder cloke vertue nat hyd moſte mortall poyſon flatterie ¶ true deſcription amitie frendeſhyp cap xi al redy treated beneuolēce beneficence generally moche frendſhyp called latin amicitia comprehēdeth thoſe vertues ſpecially hygher degree nowe ſo infrequente ſtrauuge amonge mortall men tyrannye couetyſe ambition whiche haue longe reigned yet amitie may nowe vnethe knowen founde throughoute worlde ſeke dilygently mayden wold ſeke ſmall ſyluer pynne great chaumber ſtrawed whyte ruſhes wyl therfore borow ſo moche gentyll reder thoughe nigh wery longe matter barram eloquence pleaſant ſentence declare ſomewhat way verye true frendſhyp whiche perchaunce maye allectiue good men ſeke ſemblable may practiſe amitie tulli ſaith nothinge loued ioyned togyther ſimylytude ci good maners vertues wherin ſame ſēblable ſtudies ſame wylles deſires hapneth one moch delyteth ſelfe nowe let v enſerch frendſhyp amitie ethi vi ¶ ariſtotle ſaith frendeſhyp vertue ioyneth vertue whiche affirmed tulli de amicitia tulli ſaying frendeſhyppe nat without vertue ne good men onely good men declareth thoſe perſones whiche ſo beare theym ſelues ſuche wyſe lyue faythe ſuretie equalitie lyberalitie ſufficiētly proued ne couetyſe wylfulneſſe folehardynes theym great ſtabilitie conſtance ſuppoſe taken called good men whiche doo folowe moche men maye nature chiefe capytayne guyde mannes lyfe ouer ſame tulli defyneth frendſhyppe maner ſayinge noone thynge perfect conſent al thynges appertaining aſwell god man beneuolence charitie knoweth nothing gyuen god except ſapience man cōmodious whiche definition excellent true god thynge cōmeth god nothing greatter eſtimation loue called latine amor wherof amicitia cōmeth named englyſhe frendſhyppe amitie whiche taken awaye frome lyfe man howſe ſhall abide ſtanding fyelde ſhall culture lyghtly perceyued man remembre commeth diſſention dyſcorde fynally ſeemeth take ſonne frome worlde taketh frendſhyppe mannes lyfe ¶ sen frendſhyp nat good men ne may without vertue may aſſured therof none euyl may procede therwith yuel thyng may participate wherfore moche maye fewe perſones good men ſmalle nombre alſo rare ſeldome vertues communely wyll declare opynion philoſophers partely commune experiēce amonge good men nature moſte apte frendſhippe ¶ betwene men good nat alway amitie alſo requireth ſemblable moche like maners ſtudy ſpecially maners gra uitie affabilitie euery laudable quality seueritie placabilitie alſo magnificence liberalite noble vertues yet frugalitie whiche ſobreneſſe moderation liuing good cauſe wyſe men extolled yet theſe vertues quality ſeperately ſondry perſons aſſē bled may welle perfecte concorde frendeſhyp ſeldome neuer one vertue imbraceth cōtemneth leſte neglecteth wherfore ſemeth wherein one deliteth repugnāt others nature repugnaunce may none amitie ſens frendeſhyp entier conſent wylles deſires therfore ſeldome ſene frendeſhyp betwene theſe perſons man ſturdy opinion inflexible ſoure countenance ſpeche hym tractable reaſon perſwaded ſwete coū tenance entertaynment alſo betwene hym whiche eleuate auctoritie nother baſe aſtate degree ye equall dignitie deſyrous clyme aſcende ſo frendſhyp parte decayeth tulli ſaythe fyrſte booke office thing ſo euer whiche many nat excelle haue therin ſuperiorytie therein often tymes ſuche contention thynge moſte difficile kepe amonge good vertuous company moche ſay retayne amonge frendſhyp amitie oftentymes ſene diuers came autorite good vertuous condiciōs proſperitie vtterly changed diſpiſyng old frendes ſet ſtudy pleaſure newe acquaintaunce wherin men ſhall perceyue wonderfull blyndnes mought ſay madneſſe note diligentely ſhall hereafter write frendeſhyp nowe reſorte ſpeke frenſhyp moſt frequente alſo therto moſt aptely diſpoſed ¶ undoutedly ſpecially whiche wyſe nature inclyned beneficence liberalitie conſtance wyſedome marked ſubſtancially decerned wordes actes demeanure men betwene whome hapneth entercours familiaritie whereby ingendred fauour diſpoſition loue beneficence ſaye mutually puttynge ſtudie helpe neceſſary affaire induceth loue lyberall withholde hyde nothynge loue wherby loue increſeth conſtant neuer myſtruſte ſuſpition ſurmyſe yuelle reporte drawe theym affection hereby frendeſhyppe made perpetuall ſtable yf ſimilitude ſtudy lernynge ioyned vnto ſayde vertues frendſhip moche rather hapneth mutuall enteruewe conuerſation moche pleaſaunt ſpecially ſtudies haue delectable affection motion ſerious full contention frendeſhip oftentymes aſſaulted whereby often peryll ſtudy elegant matter illecebrous ſaye ſwete reder courſe wherof rather gentyll perſwaſion quicke reaſonynges ouer ſubtyll argumente litigious controuerſyes alſo hapneth ſtudentes delyte one nother without enuye malycyous contention ¶ nowe let v try frendſhyppe ſuppoſe good men ueryly bleſſed ſtable connexyon ſondry wylles makynge two perſons one hauynge ſuffrynge therfore frende proprely named philoſophers theym one minde one poſſeſſion man reioyſeth frendes good fortune owne ¶ horeſtes pilades beinge wonderful lyke al feature taken geder preſented vnto tirant deedly hated horeſtes whan behelde bothe wolde haue ſlayne horeſtes coulde decerne one alſo pilades delyuer frende affirmed oreſtes parte oreſtes ſaue pilades denyed ſayd oreſtes trouthe thus longe tyme togyther contendynge one dye laſte ſo relented fierſe cruell harte tyraunte wondringe theyr meruaylous frendſhyp ſuffred frely departe without doinge damage ¶ pitheas damō two pythagoriens pithias damon ſay ſtudentes pythagoras lernynge beinge ioyned togyther perfect frendſhyp one accuſed haue cōſpired againſt dionyſe kyng sicile takē brought kynge immedyately gaue ſentence accuſed ſhulde put dethe deſired kinge er died mought retourne home ſet houſeholde order dyſtribute goodes whereat kyng laughynge demaunded ſkornfully pledge wolde leaue hym come agayne whiche wordes company ſtepte forthe ſayde wolde remayne pledge frend caſe came agayne daye appoynted wyllngly wold loſe hede whiche condicion tyraunte receyued yonge man ſhuld haue died ſuffred departe home hous ſet thynge order dyſpoſed goodes wyſely day appointed retourne commen tyme moche paſſed wherfore kynge called hym pledge came forth meryly without ſemblaunte drede offringe abyde ſentence tyraunte grudginge dye ſauing life frende offycer iuſtyce cloſed eien kerchiefe drawen ſwerde haue ſtryken hede felowe came renning crieng daye appoyntmente yet paſte wherfore deſired miniſter iuſtice loſe felowe prepare execution hym giuen occaſion whereat tyraunte beynge abaſhed cōmanded broughte preſence whan inough wō dred theyr noble harte theyr conſtance frendſhyp offring greate rewardes deſyred receyue hym theyr company ſo doing▪ thē moche honour dyd ſet libertie ¶ undoughtedly frendſhyp whiche doth depend eyther profite el pleſure habilitie perſone whiche mought profitable faile diminiſhe diſpoſitiō perſon ſhuld pleaſaunte chaunge appayre feruentneſſe loue ceſſeth thanne frendſhyp wonderfull hiſtory titus giſippus wherby fully declared figure perfet amitie ca xii nowe myddes labour pauſe take breth alſo recreate reders whiche fatigate longe preceptes deſyre varietic mater ſome newe pleaſaunt fable hiſtorie wyll reherce righte goodly example frendſhyp whiche example ſtudiouſely red ſhal miniſter reders ſinguler pleaſure alſo incredible comfort practiſe amitie ¶ cytie rome noble ſenatour named fuluius ſente ſonne called titus beinge chylde citie athene grece whiche fountayne al maner doctrine lerne good letter cauſed hym hoſted worſhypfull man citie called chremes chremes hapened haue alſo ſonne named giſippus onely equal ſayde yong titus yeres alſo ſtature proporcion body fauour colour viſage countenaunce ſpeche two chyldren ſo lyke without moche difficultie coulde decerned theyr propre parentes titus giſippus giſippus titus theſe two yonge gentyllmen ſemed one fourme perſonage ſo ſhortely acquaintaunce ſame nature wrought theyr harte ſuche mutuall affection theyr wylles appetite dayly ſo cōfederated ſelues ſemed none whan theyr name declared chaunged theyr place iſſuing mought ſay one body entringe gether one tyme wente theyr lernynge ſtudye one tyme theyr meales refectyon delyted bothe one doctrine profyted equally therin fynally gether ſo increaſed doctrine within fewe yeres fewe within athene mought compared vnto laſte dyed chremes whiche onely lonne alſo titus cauſe moche ſorowe heuyneſſe gyſippus goodes father knowen manne great ſubſtaunce wherfore offred hym greate ryche mariages rype yeres habile goodly perſonage frendes kinne alies exhorted hym buſely take wyfe entent mought increaſe lynage progenye yonge man hauyng harte redy wedded frende titus minde fixed ſtudy philoſophie ferynge maryage ſhulde occaſion ſeuer thone thother refuſed longe tyme perſwaded vntyll laſte partly importunate callynge kynneſmenne partely conſente aduyſe dere frende titus therto deſired aſſented mary ſuche one ſhulde lyke ſhall nede wordes frendes found yonge gentyl woman whiche equalitie yeres vertuous condicions nobilitie blode beaute ſufficiente richeſſe thought ſuche yonge man apt conueniente whan frē de vpon cōuenantes mariage throughely accorded counſayled giſippus repayre vnto mayden beholde howe perſone contented ſoo doynge founde euerye fourme condicion according expectation apperite whereat moche reioyſed became amorouſe ſoo moche many often tymes leauing titus ſtudy ſecretely repaired vnto ſtandynge feruent loue frende titus laſt ſurmounted ſhamefaſtnes wherfore dyſcloſed hym ſecrete iourneyes delectacion toke beholding excellent beautie purpoſed marye howe good maners ſwete enterteynemente ſhe conſtrayned hym louer tyme hauynge hym frende titus wente lady reſceyued moſte ioyouſly titus furthewith behelde ſo heuenly perſonage adourned beautie inexplicable whoſe viſage mooſte amiable countenaunce myxt maydenly ſhamefaſteneſſe rare ſobre wordes well couched whiche iſſued pretye mouthe titus therat abaſhed harte perced firy darte blynde cupide whiche wounde anguiſhe ſo excedyng vehement neyther ſtudy philoſophie neyther remēbrance dere frende giſippus ſo moche loued truſted hym coulde thyng drawe hym vnkynde appetite force muſte loue inordinately lady ſaide frende determined mary al incredible paynes kepte thoughtes ſecrete vntyll giſippus returned vnto theyr lodgynges myſerable titus withdrawynge hym ſtudye turmented oppreſſed loue threwe hym ſelfe bed rebukyng owne moſte deſpitefull vnkyndneſſe ſodeyne ſyghte mayden conſpired agaynſte mooſte dere frende giſippus agaynſt humanitie reaſō curſed fate conſtellation wiſſhed neuer comen athene therwith ſente botome harte depe colde ſyghes ſuche plentie lacked litel hart ne ryuen peces dolour anguiſhe toſſed ſelfe certain ſpace man wolde dyſcouer laſte peyne became ſo intollerable wold inforced kepe bed beinge lacke ſlepe naturall ſuſtenaunce broughte ſuche febleneſſe legges mougt ſuſteine body giſippus miſſynge dere frēd titus moche abaſſhed herynge laye ſycke bed forthwith harte perced heuyneſſe ſpede came hym laye beholdynge roſiall colour whiche wonte viſage tourned ſalowe reſydue pale ruddy lyppes wan eyen ledy holowe moughte vneth kepe hym ſelfe wepyng entente wolde dyſcomforte frende titus diſſimuled heuyneſſe comfortable countenaunce demaunded titus cauſe diſeaſe blamynge hym vnkyndeneſſe ſo longe ſuſteyned without gyuinge hym knowlege moughte hym haue prouyded ſome remedye mought haue begoten though dyſpendynge ſubſtaunce wordes mortal ſyghes renewed titus ſalte teares braſte eyen ſuche habundaunce ben lande flode runnyng downe moū tayne ſtorme beholdyng giſyppns beinge alſo reſolued teares moſte hartely deſired hym mought ſay coniured feruente entier loue bene yet betwene wold lenger hide hym gryefe nothynge hym ſo deere precyous though owne life mought reſtore titus helthe ſhulde gladly without grutchynge employe whiche wordes obteſtations teares gyſippus titus conſtrayned al bluſſhynge aſſhamed holdinge downe hede brought furthe greate difficultie wordes wiſe ¶ dere moſte louyng frende wordes titus giſyppus drawe frendely offer ceſſe courtaiſie refraine teares regretynges take rather knyfe ſlee lye otherwyſe take vengeaunce mooſte miſerable falſe traytour vnto mooſte worthy ſuffre moſt ſhameful deathe god nature like hath giuen v ſimilitude partes body ſo conioyned wylles ſtudies appetite gether one ſo betwene two men neuer like concorde loue ſuppoſe ſtandynge loke woman thoſe bondes loue dyſſolued reaſon oppreſſed frēdſhip excluded auaileth wyſedome doctrine fidelite truſte ye truſte cauſe haue conſpired agaynſte treaſon ala gyſippus enuious ſpirite mened bringe whō ye haue choſen wyfe receyued poyſon ſaye gyſyppus wyſedom ye remembred fragilitie cōmune nature neded cal witneſſe priuate delites wolde ye haue ſee whiche ſelfe coulde beholde without rauyſſhyng mynde carnall appetite ala forgate ye myndes appetite euer one alſo ſoo ye lyked euer lyke degree pleaſaunte wyll ye gyſippus ſaye truſt cauſe intrapped rayes beames iſſuynge eyen ye haue choſen remē braunce incomparable vertues hath thrilled throughout middes hart ſuche wyſe brenneth aboue althinges deſire wretched moſte vnkinde life whiche worthy company ſo noble louynge frende ye therwith titus concluded confeſſion ſo profound bytter ſighe receyued teares ſemed body ſhulde dyſſolued relented ſalte dropes ¶ gyſippus therwith nothynge annſwere giſippus aſtonyed dyſcontented aſſured countenannce mery regarde imbraſynge titus kyſſynge hym anſwerd wiſe titus ſickeneſſe griefe ye ſo vncur • eſely haue ſo longe counceyled moch vnkindneſſe kept ye haue conceiued knowlege foly wherwith ye haue good right imbraided ſhewyng loued remembred commune aſtate nature ne agreableneſſe moughte ſaye vnitie two appetite suerly defaulte reaſon excuſed wherfore onely haue offended may ryght proue ye haue treſpaſed ineuitable ſtroke cupides dart thus bytterly wounded thynke ye ſuche ſole ignorant perſone knowe power uenus ſhe lyſteth ſhewe importable vyolence haue ye wel reſyſted agaynſte ſuche goddeſſe ſake haue ſtryuen mooſte deathe loyaltye trouthe require vertue maye reſyſte agaynſt celeſtiall influence preordynate prouydence dyuine ſo thought wyttes ſtudy ſo longe time ſpent noble philoſophy confeſſe titus loue mayden moche wyſe man mought poſſyble toke company delyte pleaſure al treaſure landes father lefte whiche ye knowe ryght abundaunte nowe perceyue affection loue towarde ſurmouuteth aboue meaſure ſhall thynke wanton luſte ſodeyne appetite haue euer knowē graue ſadde dyſpoſytion inclyned alwaye honeſt doctrine fleynge al vayne dalyaunce dyſhoneſte paſſetyme shal imagine malice fraude ſens tender tyme chyldehode haue alwaye founden ſwete frende titus ſuche conformytye maners appetite deſires neuer ſeene betwene v maner contention nay god forbede frendſhyppe gyſyppus titus ſhoulde happen ſuſpition fantaſye ſhulde perce hedde wherby honourable loue betwene v ſhulde mountenaunce cromme peryſſhed nay nay titus haue ſaid onely prouydence god ſhe hym begynnynge prepared lady wyfe ſuch feruent loue entreth harte wyſe manne vertuous dyuyne dyſpoſyton whereat yf ſhoulde dyſcontented▪ grudge ſhulde iniuſte holdynge vndoubtedly alſo obſtinate repugnant agaynſt determination god whiche ſhal neuer founden giſyppus therfore gentyll frende titus dyſmaye chaunce loue receyue ioyously nothinge diſcontented meruaylous glad ſens happe finde ſuche lady whome ye ſhall lyue felicitie receyue fruite honour comfort lynage renounce clerely al title intereſt nowe haue mought haue fayre mayden call priſtinate courage waſhe clene viſage eien thus bywepte abandone heuyneſſe day apointed mariage approcheth let v cō ſulte howe without dyfficultie ye may holy attayne deſyres take hede myne aduiſe ye knowe wel two ſo lyke beinge parte one apparayle fewe men knowe v alſo ye remembre cuſtome withſtandynge ceremony one tyme ſpouſayles maryage notwithſtandynge confyrmed vntyll night huſbande putteth rynge finger wife vnloſeth apparayle ye ſhall eſpyed woman haue none v acqueyntaunce ſhortely get bed put owne rynge maydens fynger vndo gyrdell virginitie thynge ſhalbe pleaſure nowe good chere titus comforte ſelfe good refection ſolace wanne pale colour chekes meygre leane cauſe diſcouering knowe wel ye hauing purpoſe ſhall obloquie deriſion men ſoo hated kynrede ſhall ſeke occaſion expulſe citie thynkynge notable reproch familie let god therin warke force payne abyde ſoo ye frende titus may ſaulfe pleaſauntly enioye deſyres increaſynge felicitie ¶ vvith theſe wordes titus beganne meue dreme doubtynge whether harde giſyppus ſpeke elles ſawe viſyon lay ſtyll man abaſhed whan behelde teares tryckelynge downe face gyſyppus recomforted hym thankyng hym incomparable kyndneſſe refuſed benefyte offered ſayinge better hundred ſuche vnkynde wretch ſhulde peryſſhe ſoo noble manne gyſippus ſhulde ſuſteyne reproche damage gyſyppus eſteſones comforted titus therwith ſware proteſted fre gladde wyl wold thynge ſhulde fourme aforeſayde accomplyſſhed therwith inbraced ſwetely kyſſed titus perceiuynge matter ſure feyned man ſycke awaked flepe ſet hym ſelfe vp bed quicke bloud ſome reſorted vnto vyſage lyttell good meates drinkes taken ſhortely fewe dayes reſtored old facion figure make tale ſhorte daye maryage commen gyſyppus accompanied alies frendes came houſe damoſell honorably ioyouſly feſted betwene mayden ſwete entertaynemente whiche beholde preſente toke moche pleaſure comfort prayſing beautie goodlyneſſe vertue curteſie couple excellent aboue hadde euer ſene ſhal ſay couenātes radde ſealed dowar apointed bargaynes concluded frendes either parte toke leaue depted bride fewe woman cuſtome brought chambre thā agreed titus conueyed hym ſelfe gyſippus retourned houſe perchance chambre appointed titus nothyng ſorowfull although hartily loued mayden gladde harte countenaunce hadde ſo recouered frende deth ſo well broughte hym effecte deſyre nowe titus bedde mayden knowen gyſippus fyrſte ſweetely demaunded ſhe loued dayned take hym huſbāde forſakyng whiche ſhe al bluſhing eye halfe laughynge halfe mournynge poynte depart frō maidenheed ſuppoſinge gyſippus aſked affirmed efteſones aſketh ſhe ratifieng ꝓmiſe wold receyue ryng alredy wherto ſhe conſentyng putteth rynge fynger vnloſeth gyrdell thynge el dyd two knewe one thynge ſure nyghte titus comfortable euer lengeſt daye yere ye ſuppoſe hoole yere dayes morowe comen gyſippus thinking expedient trouth ſhuld diſcouered aſſembled nobilitie citie owne houſe alſo appoyntemente titus amonge theſe wordes folowe ¶ frendes atheniēſis oration titus athenienſis tyme ſhewed amonge example almoſt incredible diuine powar honorable loue perpetuall renome cōmendatiō noble cite athene wherof ye ought take excellent cōfort therfore gyue due thankes god ther remayne amonge token ancient wyſedome moſte noble progenitours prayſe maye giuen people thā beneuolence faithfulneſſe conſtance withoute whome countrayes city brought vnto deſolation ruyne like come proſperous mooſte high felilicitie ſhall longe tary coniectyng myne intent meanynge ye know whens came vnto citie auēture foūd hous chre me ſonne gyſippus min owne age euery thing ſo lyke neyther father man coulde diſcerne v one frome owne inſignement ſhewynge ſo moch put neckes lacis ſondry colour daclare perſonages mutuall agrement loue haue ben alwaye betwene v durynge eyght yeres haue ben togither ye witneſſes haue ben beholder wonderars moſt ſwete conuerſation cōſent appetite wherin neuer diſcorde variaunce part deceſſe father natwith ſtandinge diſcended hapned vnto great poſſeſſiōs fayre houſes abundance rich alſo called home deſirous importunate let ters myn alies frendes moſte noble ſenatours offred aduancement higheſt dignity publike weale wyll nat remembre lamentation moſte naturall mother expreſſed tender letter ſprent blotted abūdāce ofteares wherin ſhe accuſeth vnkyndneſſe longe taryenge ſpeciallye nowe moſte diſcomforte coulde nat remoue breadthe naylle frome dere frende gyſippus force coulde nat yet may drawen ſwete cōpany yf therto wylle conſente chooſynge rather lyue hym company felowe ye ſeruaunt rather conſull rome thus kyndenes hath wel acquyted mought ſay redoubled delyueryng deth ye moſte cruel peynefull deth perceyue ye wonder hereat noble athenienſis noo meruayle perſon ſhulde ſo hardy attempte ſuche thyng ageynſt romayne noble blode romaynes ſhulde thought ſo malicious ſlee ye iuges neuer treſpaſſed agaynſte perſone within citie nay nay frēdes haue none therin ſuſpected perceyue ye deſyre harken knowe preſumed ſo cruell great enterpriſe loue noble athenienſis ſame loue poetes doo remembre dydde wounde parte goddis ye doo honour conſtrayaed iupiter tranſfourme hym ſelfe ſwanne bulle dyuers likeneſſes ſame loue cauſed hercules vaynquyſher diſtroyer monſters giauntes ſpinne rocke ſyttynge amonge maydens womannes apparayle ſame loue cauſed aſſemble noble pryncis aſia grece fieldes troy ſame loue ſaye agaynſte whoſe aſſaultes may founde defence reſiſtēce hath ſodainely vnware ſtryken vnto harte ſuche vehemence myghte ſhorte ſpace dyed moſte feruent tourmentes hadde nat incomparable frendſhip gyſippus holpen ſee wolde fayne knowe ſhe loued wyll lenger delaye noble athenienſis sophronia lady gyſippus choſen haue wyfe whome moſte entierly loued whan mooſte gentyll harte perceyued loue moche hygher degree toward lady proceded neither wantōnes neyther longe conuerſation corrupte deſyre fantaſie inſtant onely looke ſuche feruence īmediatly ſo cruciate deſired mought prouoked deth take wiſedom ſo one perceyued doute nat ye prouiſiō god ſhe ſhuld wyfe nat wherto giuynge place eſtemyng true frendſhip loue woman wher vnto induced frendes nat violence cupide cōſtrayned hath willyngly graunted intereſt hadde damoſell titus haue verily weded haue putte rynge fynger haue vndo one gyrdell ſhame faſtenes wylle ye haue lyen confyrmed matrymonye made wyfe ¶ theſe wordes preſent began murmure caſte diſdainous greuous loke vpon giſippus ſpake ageyne titus ¶ leave yovr grudgynges menaſynge countenaunce towarde gyſyppus hath doone honour dede reproche telle hath accomplyſhed partes frende loue whyche mooſte certayne hath contynued knew mought fynd greece maiden faire ryche choſen one perchaunce mought loue better ſuche frende hauyng reſpect ſimilitude longe approued concorde alſo myne aſtate condytion ſure fynde neuer none alſo damoſell ſuffereth diſper gemente hyr bloode hynderance mariage moche rather aduaunced dyſpreyſe dere frende gyſippus alſo cōſider noble athenienſis toke nat father lyuynge whan ye mought haue ſuſpected well ryches beautie ſhoulde haue therto allured ſoone father deceaſe whan far exceded poſſeſſions ſubſtance whan moſte notable men rome italy deſired myn aliāce ye haue therfore cauſe reioyſe thanke gyſippus nat angry alſo extoll wonderfulle kyndeneſſe towarde wherby hath wonne al blode ſuche frendes cytie ye may aſſured v defended agaynſt worlde whiche beinge conſidered giſippus hath well deſerued ſtatue ymage golde ſet piller myddes citie honorable monumente remembraunce incomparable frēdſhyp good therby may come citie perſuaſion nat ſatiſfie ye wyll imagyne thyng damage dere frende gyſippus departynge make myne auowe vnto god creatour thynge ſhall haue knowlege therof ſhall furth reſorte hyther inuyncible power romaynes reuenge ſuche wyſe againſt enmies al grece ſhal ſpeke perpetuall diſhonour ſhame reproche ¶ therwith titus gyſippus rooſe feare titus diſſembled malyce makynge ſemblaunt ben thynge contented ¶ sone titus beinge ſent auctorite ſenate peple rome prepared departe athene wolde faine haue hadde gyſippus haue goone hym offrynge deuyde hym ſubſtance fortune gyſippus conſiderynge howe neceſſarye counſayle ſhuld citie athene wolde nat depart countray nat withſtandynge aboue erthly thynges moſt deſired company titꝰ whiche abode alſo ſayd conſideration titus approued ¶ titus lady departed towardes citie rome cō mynge mother titus kynſemen al ſenate people ioyouſly receyued liued titus lady ioye inexplycable many faire child wyſedome lernynge ſo hyghely eſtemed dignitie honorable offyce within citie hadde moche fauour prayſe chyeued occupied ¶ let v reſorte giſippus immediately vpon departing titus ſoo malygned well owne kynſemen frendes ladye theyr ſemynge ſhamefully abandoned lcauynge titus ſpared dayly vexe hym kyndes reproche coulde deuyſe imagine fyrſte excluded hym theyr counſayle prohibited hym al honeſt company yet therewith ſatisfyed fynally adiuged hym vnworthy enioye poſſeſſions goodes left hym parentes whō ſuppoſed vndeſcrete frendſhyppe ſo dyſtayned wherfore dyſpoyled hym thynges almoſte naked expelled citie thus gyſippus late welthy one mooſte noble men athene kynde harte banyſſhed owne countrey euer man dyſmayed wandring hyther thyther fyndynge man wolde ſocour hym laſt remembring pleſure frend titus liued lady ſuffred theſe damage concluded go rome declare infortune ſaid frend titus ſhall nede longe tale concluſyon moche peyne colde hunger thurſte commen citie rome diligently enquiringe houſe titus laſte came beholdinge ſo beauteous large pryncely aſhamed approche nygh beynge ſo ſymple aſtate vnklad ſtandeth caſe titus came forth howſe moughte preſente hym ſelfe hym beynge thoughte titus holdynge lady hande iſſued doore takynge theyr horſes ſolace ſelfe beheld giſyppus beholdynge vyle apparayle regarded hym paſſed furthe theyr waye wherewith gyſippus ſoo wounded harte thynkynge titus contempned fortune oppreſſed mortal heuynes fell ſowne beynge recouered ſome ſtode thynkyng ſyeke furth departed entending abide lenger wilde beaſt wander abrode worlde werineſſe conſtrayned entre olde barne without citie caſtinge ſelfe bare gronde wepynge dolorous cryenge bewayled fortune moſte accuſynge ingratitude titus ſuffred myſery remembraunce wherof ſo intollerable determined lenger lyue anguyſhe dolour therwith drewe knyfe purpoſyng haue ſlayne hym ſelfe euer wyſedome whiche ſtudy philoſophy attayned withdrewe hym frome deſperate acte contentiō betwene wyſedome wyll fatigate long iournaies watche god wold haue fell dede ſlepe knyfe wherwith wolde haue ſlayne ſelfe fallyng downe hym meane time commune notable rufyan thefe whiche hadde robbed ſlayne manne entred barne gyſyppus laye intente ſoiorne nyghte ſeyng giſippus bewept viſage replenyſſhed ſorowe alſo naked knyfe hym perceyued well man deſperate ſuppriſed heuyneſſe harte werye lyfe whiche ſayde rufyan takynge good occaſion eſcape toke knyfe gyſyppus puttynge wounde hym ſlayne put blody hande gyſyppus beinge faſte ſlepe ſo departed soone dedde man beinge founde officer made dyligente ſerche murderar laſte entringe barne fyndinge giſippus ſlepe blody knife hande awaked hym wherwith entred agayne olde ſorowes complaynynge yuel fortune whan officer layde vnto death man hauynge blody knyfe thereat reioyſed thankynge god ſuche occaſiō hapned wherby ſhuld ſuffre deathe lawes eſcape vyolence owne handes wherfore denyed nothynge layde charge deſyryng officer make haſt mought ſhortely lyfe whereat meruayled anone reporte came ſenate man ſlayne ſtraunger greeke borne founde ſuche fourme mencioned forthwith commaunded hym brought vnto theyr preſence ſittynge tyme titus conſull lyke dignitie miſerable giſippus brought barr̄ billes ſtaues like felon demaunded ſlewe man foundended nothynge denyed moſt ſorowfull maner curſed fortune namynge hym ſelfe moſte miſerable laſte one demaundynge hym coūtrey confeſſed athenienſe therwith caſt ſorowfull eyen vppon titus moche indignation braſte oute ſyghes teares abundauntly beholdynge titus eſpienge lyttel ſygne viſage knewe dere frende giſyppus anone conſideringe brought dyſpayre ſome ſaduenture roſe place ſate falling knee iuges ſayd ſlayne man olde malyce bare towarde gyſippus ſtraunger giltles men mought perceyue deſperate perſon wherfore abbreuiate ſorowes confeſſed acte wherof innocent intent wold finiſhe ſorowes deth wherfore titus deſyred iuges giue ſentence hym accordynge merytes gyſippus perceyuynge frēde titus contrary expectation offre hym ſelfe deathe ſaulfe garde importunately cried ſenate procede theyr iugement hym offēdar titus denied affirmed reaſons argumētes murderer giſyppus thus longe tyme abundaunce teares contēded ſhuld die wherat senate people wonderly abaſſhed knowyng ment murderer dede hapned preaſe time perceiuing meruaylous contention theſe two perſones bothe innocēt proceded incō parable frendſhip vehemently prouoked dyſcouer trouthe wherfore brake preaſe cōminge ſenate ſpake wiſe ¶ noble father ſuch perſō ye knowe haue ben cōmune baratour thefe long ſpace yeres ye know alſo titus noble bloude proued alway man excellent vertue wyſedome neuer malycious ſtrāger ſemeth mā full ſimplicitie deſperate ſome greuous ſorowe hath taken euidente ſay father innocente perſon ſlewe hym foundēded barne robbed money whan founde barne ſtranger lyenge ſlepe hauinge hym naked knyfe better hyde myne offence dyd put knife wounde ded man ſo al blody laide agayne ſtranger miſcheuous deuiſe eſcape iugement vnto nowe remit holy rather noble man titus innocent ſtranger ſhulde vnworthely die ¶ senate people toke comforte noiſe reioyſing harte filled courte whan examined giſippus dyſcouered frendſhip betwene hym titus citie publyſſhed extolled magnified wherfore senate conſulted mater fynally inſtāce titus peple dyſcharged felon titus recognyſed neglygence forgettynge giſippus titus beinge aduertiſed exile giſippus dipiteful crueltie kynrede therwith wonderfull wrath hauinge giſippus home hous incredible ioye receiued lady ſomtyme ſhulde haue wedded honorably apparyled titus offred hym vſe al goodes poſſeſſiōs owne pleaſure appetite giſippus deſyrynge agayne propre countrey titus conſente senate people aſſembled gret army wente gyſyppus vnto athene hauing deliuered al thoſe whiche cauſers banyſſhynge dyſpoylynge frende gyſyppus dyd ſharpe execution reſtorynge gyſyppus landes ſubſtance ſtablyſhed hym perpetuall quietnes ſo retourned rome ¶ exaumple affectes frendſhyp expreſſeth deceyued deſcription frendeſhyppe engendred ſymilitude age perſonage augmented conformitie maners ſtudies confirmed longe continuance company ¶ wolde remembred frendſhip none euil maye frendſhip betwene good men onely ingendred opinion vertue may reaſon fourme good man ſo named bycauſe wylleth doth good good none euyl therfore nothynge good man wylleth dothe euyl lykewyſe vertue affection good man neither willeth dothe thynge euyl vice contrary vnto vertue opinion vertue neyther euyll vyce amytie vertue wherfore nothynge euyll vycyous maye happen frendſhyp therfore fyrſte election frendes reſteth al importāce wherfore wold without longe beliberation profe ariſtotle ſayth ethie longe tyme bothe beinge gether conuerſaunt hole buſſhell ſalte mought eten oftentymes fortune late ſayd chaunged leaſt miniſhed feruentneſſe affection according ſwete poete duide affirmeth ſayinge ſentence ¶ while fortune fauoureth frendes thou oui de pon haſt plentie tyme beinge troublous thou arte al alone thou ſeeſt coluers haunte houſes made whyte dente ruynous towre moſte cometh none emotes innumerable vneth thou findeſt one emty barnes fayleth ſubſtaunce hapneth frende aſſuraunce ¶ hapneth euerye fortune conſtant frendſhippe made aboue thynges maye come vnto man aboue bloude kynrede tulli ſayth kynrede maye taken beneuolence frome frendſhippe neuer ſeuered wherfore beneuolence taken kynrede yet name kynſeman remayneth take frendſhyp name frendſhip vtterly peryſhed ¶ ſens liberte ſpeche nowe howe diſcernea frēd flatterer vſurped flaterers perceiue aſſentation praiſes abhorred therfore well aſſured howe man nowe dayes ſhal knowe dyſcerne ſuche admonicion flatery one onely meanes ſaye remembre frēdſhip maye betwene good mē conſider doth admonyſſhe hym ſelfe voluptuous ambicious couetous arrogant diſſolute refuſe admonicion example emperour antonine thākefully take amende ſuche defaulte thou perceyueſte doth gyue occaſion obloqui ſuche maner reporter alſo thyne exaumple maye corrected admonicion onely accompt hym immediatly thy frend vntyl thou haue hym lōge ſure experience vndoubtedly wonderful difficile fynde man ambitious couetous aſſured frendſhyp fyndeſt thou hym ſaythe tulli wyl prefer honoures great office rule autoritie rycheſſe frendſhyp therfore ſayth harde fynde frendſhyp occupied acquiring honour affayres publyke weale ſayinge proued trewe dayly experience dyſdayne contempt companiōs ambition lyke enuye hatered alſo folowers diuiſion ingratitude dyſprayſe therof ca xiii moſt damnable vice moſte agaynſt iuſtice myn opinion ingratitvde commenly called vnkindneſſe diuers formes ſondry importaunce diſcrybed seneca fourme ¶ vnkynde whiche denyeth haue receyued benefite dede hath receyued vnkynde diſſimuleth vnkynde recompenſeth moſte vnkynde forgetteth though render agayne kindneſſe yet owe remaineth ſome ſteppes tokēs deſertes incloſed yuel conſcience laſte ſome occaſion maye hap retourne yelde agayne thankes whan eyther ſhame therto prouoketh ſodeyne deſyre thynge honeſt whiche wonte tyme ſtomackes thoughe corrupted lyghte occaſyon moue forgetteth kindeneſſe maye neuer kynde ſens al benefite quite fallen hym lacketh remembraunce hope recompence ¶ vice men moche warſe kyndenes beſtis beaſtes dyuers wyl remembre benefytte longe receyued courſer fierſe couragious wyll gladely ſuf • keper dreſſeth fedeth hym vaunte hym eaſely ſtereth whan lyſtethe prouoke hym ſhulde ryde hym thoughe kynge wyl ſtere plonge endeuour hym ſelfe throwe hym suche kyndeneſſe hath ben founden kidnes dogges dogges haue dyed defendynge theyr mayſters alſo ſome theyr maiſters haue died ben ſlaine haue abſteyned meate famine haue dyed theyr mayſters ¶ plini remembreth dogge whiche epiro contrey grece ſo aſſaulted murdrer mayſter great aſſembly people barkynge bytynge compelled hym laſte confeſſe offence ¶ dogge alſo one iayſon maiſter beinge ſlayne wolde neuer eate meate dyed hunger ¶ many ſēblable token kindneſſe plini reherſeth principally one tyme worthy remembred ¶ whan execution ſhoulde done one titus habinius ſeruantes one dogge whiche moughte neuer dryuen pryſon neuer wold departe mayſters body whā taken place executiō dogge houled mooſte lamentably beynge compaſed great nombre people whan one caſt meate dogge brought laide mouthe maiſter whā corp throwen ryuer tiber dogge ſwamme longe moughte inforced hym ſelfe beare ſuſteyne people ſcateryng abrode beholde faythfulneſſe beaſte ¶ alſo lyon whiche beaſtes accounted mooſte fierce cruell hath ben founden haue remembraunce benefite ſhewed vnto hym ¶ aul bellius remembreth hyſtory appion howe allon whoſe fote yonge man one taken ſtubbe clenſed wounde wherby waxed hole knewe ſame man caſt deuoured wolde hurt hym lyckynge legges handes man whiche laye dyſmayde lokinge deathe toke acquaintaunce euer folowed hym beynge ladde ſmall lyam whereat wondred behelde whiche hyſtorie wonderfull pleaſaunte lengthe therof conſtrayned abrege ¶ howe moche repugnaunte moughte ſaye ennemies bothe nature reaſon whiche beynge aduaunced good fortune wyll contemne neglecte ſuche one haue longe knowē beneuolent ioyned ſincere aſſured frendſhyppe approued infallible token ratifyed alſo ſondry kyndes benefycence require ſuche excellant frendſhyppe betwene pitheas damon betwene horeſtes pilades twene gyſyppus titus whome haue wrytten fyrmely beleue ſhall neuer happen payres couple ſeke ſuche alway prefer honour profyte theyr frēde theyr owne ne leaſte parte frendſhyppe ſuch one deſirouſly wyll participate frende good fortune ſubſtaunce daye maye founden ſuche frendſhyppe betwene two fortune frēdſhip tyme beneuolente one frendeſhyppe waxeth tedyous aduaunced deſyrethe matched one hauynge ſemblable fortune damage hapeneth olde frende pytyeth hym ſoroweth thoughe ſeeme ſorowfull yet helpeth thoughe wolde ſene helpe hym yet trauaileth nat though wolde ſene trauayle yet ſuffreth let v laye parte aſſyſtence moneye whyche ſmall portion frendeſhyp wyll ſo moche eſteme frendſhyp therefore wyll entre dyſpleaſure prynce whome ſuppoſeth may mynyſſhe eſtimation towardes prince ye moche leſſe wyll diſpleaſe newe acquayntaunce equall hym auctorite fortune defence helpe aduauncement auncient well approued frende moſte miſcrable aſtate preſent tyme mankynde thynge whiche mooſte propre vnto exaumple muſte founden amonge ſauage ſyerce beaſtes election frendes diuerſite flaterers cap xiiii noble man aboue thynge oughte circumſpecte electiō ſuche men ſhulde continually attende vpon perſone tymes vacante buſye affayres maye vſe familiar ſaufely commytte thē ſecretes plutarche ſaith ſo euer loueth doteth blynde thynge whiche dothe plutarchꝰ de cognoſcēdo amico ab adulatore loue excepte lernyng accuſtome hym ſelfe enſue ſette pryce thoſe thynges honeſte vertuous ſeeth experyence familiarly vſed ſuerly wormes brede mooſte gladly ſofte wode ſwete ſo mooſte gentyll noble wyttes inclined honour repleniſhed moſt honeſt curtaiſe maners ſoneſt admytte flaterars abuſed meruayle lyke wylde corne beinge ſhape greatneſſe lyke good mengled great difficultie wyll tryed either narowe holed ſeeue wyl ſtil abide good corne orelles hole large wyll iſſue ſoo flattery frendſhyppe hardely ſeuered moche euery motion affect minde mutually mengled together peruerſe curſed people ſondry kindes apparantly flatter prayſynge extollynge euery thing done theyr ſuperior bearynge hande hym euery man commended trouthe al men abhorred hated affyrmaunce wherof adde othes adiurations horrible curſes offryng ſelfes eternal peynes except theyr reporte true perceiue parte theyr tale miſtruſted thā ſette forthe ſodeynely heuy ſorowfull countenaunce abiected brought extreme deſperation honeſt terme maye called aſſentatours folowers whiche awayte diligently fourme ſpeche geſture theyr mayſter alſo maners facion garmentes imytatiō reſemblaunce therof applie theyr ſtudy ſimylitude maners maye rather accepted famyliar habite philoſopher therby encreaſynge kynges fauour towardes holy gyuen ſtudy philoſophye dionyſe theyr incitation hadde expelled plato sicile abandoned theyr habite ſeueritie eſtſones retourned theyr miſcheuous voluptuous lyuinge ¶ greate alexaunder bare hedde ſome parte one ſyde whiche diuers ſeruantes dyd counterfayte ¶ semblably dyd ſcholers plato moſt noble philoſopher whiche moche theyr mayſter brode breſte hygh ſhulders cauſe named plato whiche ſygnifyeth brode large ſtuffed theyr garmentes made theyr ſhulders greate bolſters ſeme like fourme wherby ſhulde conceyue ſome fauour towardes demōſtration loue pretēded oſtentation perſon kinde flatery ſuppoſe plato coulde right well laugh ¶ theſe maner flaterars may well founde perceyued good witte whiche ſometyme hym ſelfe dyligentely conſidereth owne quality natural appetite company communication perſon familiar whiche alwaye pleaſaunte without ſharpnes inclinyng inordinate fauour affection alway ſuſpected ¶ alſo frende ſmall cōmoditie whiche foloweth man lyke ſhadowe meuynge whan meueth abiding liſt tary theſe mortall enemyes noble wyttes ſpecially youthe whanne communely inclined glory grauite wherfore liberalitie ſuche flaterers imployed onely periſhed alſo ſpilled deuoured wherfore myne opinion right neceſſary lawe ſhulde made put ſuche perſons openly torture fearefull exaumple ſens pryncys lawes pytcheth haye nette woode amonge greatte tree thornes mooſte haunte lyon beinge blynded thyckenes couerte maye er ware ſodeynely tumble nette hunter ſeelynge bothe eyen byndinge legges ſtrongly gether frownyng gruching euery thing wherin myrth ſolace though honeſt tauntynge rebukyug immoderately whome cō tented namyng ſelfes therfore plain men althoughe ſemblable often tymes warſe theyr owne howſes ſimplicitie rudeneſſe ſpeakynge longe delyberation vſed ſame pretende hygh knowlege coū ſayle onely wyſe pytchynge theyr net adulation intrap noble vertuous harte whiche onely beholdeth theyr numbre eyen eares handes legges conſiderynge one man maye ſee thynge many men may ſe ne place many thynges well one tyme many perſōs maye often time beholder loker eſpieth defaulte doer forgetteth ſkyppeth ouer whiche cauſed emperour antonine ēquire many men ſpake hym correctinge therby defautes whiche perceyued iuſtely reproued ¶ truſte ſhal ſuffiſe expreſſynge incomparable treaſure called amytie declaration wherof haue aboden longer intente perſwade reders enſerche therfore vigilantly beinge ſo happy fynde accordinge ſayde deſcription embrace honour abhorrynge aboue thynges ingratytude whiche peſtylence hath longe tyme raygned amonge v augmented detraction corrupte lothly ſyckeneſſe wherof wyll trayte laſte parte warke men good nature eſpienge nede liſt therwith deceyued finis libri commendable ne wytte maner doctryne profytable tulli offic frō whēs name kynge fyrſte proceded ſaithe beginninge whan multitude people opreſſed abounded poſſeſſions ſubſtance eſpienge ſome one people ſhall appere example enſuynge ¶ whan valyaunte kinge pyrrus warred moſte aſprely agaynſte romaynes treaſon hated enemy one timochares whoſe ſonne yomā mouthe kynge promyſed fabricius conſul embraced equytie well ſlewe theyr enemye treaſon alſo betrayed hym whiche purpoſed kyndnes ¶ ſo moche iuſtice olde tyme eſtemed without none acte alowed neuer ſo noble profitable ¶ tyme xerxes kynge perſya honeſtye preferred cō moditie army expulſed grece nauye lacedemonia laye rode hauen called gytheum within minion athenienſis themiſtocles one princis athene moche noble capitayne ſayde vnto people aduyſed hym ſelfe excellente counſayle vnto fortune inclyned nothynge mought augment power athenienſis aught diuulgate publyſhed therfore deſyred haue one appoynted vnto hym mought ſecretly credence mought ſaye become vagabounde ¶ ioſue ſucceded moyſes gouernance leadyng iewes almighty god gaue cōmaundement ſle many ſhulde happen take people called cananees hapned autoritie fidelitie cō firmed leage ſolempne othe ratified one afterwarde dyſcouered cananees ioſue knowen leage made ſpared whē reuolued mind ſolempne othe made honour conſiſted promiſe preſumed faythe beinge obſerued
