tyme saul greuous offence faythfulnes ſubiectes abandoned myghtye god poore mannes ſonne god ausunced kyngedome iſrael dauid beyng ſeruant poore mannes ſonne elected god reigne iſrael enointed kynge prophet samuell saul therfore rage hauing indjgnation dauid pur ſued hym great hooſt haue ſlayne long mought fled forbare saul ſoueraigne lord tyme dauid ſo incloſed armye saul mought wais eſcape fayne hyde hym men great caue whiche wyde depe erthe durynge tyme caue saul knowinge therof entred caue naturall eaſement whiche people dauid perceyuinge exhorted hym ſlee saul hauinge ſuch oportunitie ſaying god brought ennemy handes saul ſlayne warre ende conſiderynge people lo ued better dauid thanne saul dauid refuſynge theyr counſayle ſayde wolde laye violent handes ſoueraygne lord beinge kynge enoynted god ſoftely approched saul cutte peace nether parte mantell saul departed caue toward campe dauid called ſaying purſueſt thou noble prynce wordes reherſed bible fyrſte boke kinges ſhewed hym parte mantell whereat saul abaſhed recogniſed vnkindneſſe callynge dauid dere ſonne truſty frende recommendynge hym chyldren progenye ſens wyl god elected ſuccede hym kyngedome iſrael ſoo departed saul dauid ¶ yet withſtandynge afterwarde purſued hym gaddy nyghte whan saul armye reſt dauid eſpiall knewe faſte ſlepe toke hym certayne moſte aſſured valiaunte perſonages hoſte moſte ſecrete wyſe came pauilion kynge saul founde hym ſlepynge hauynge hym ſpeare cup water wherfore one company dauid ſayde ſpeare saul wolde ſtryke hym throughe ſlee nay ſayde dauid lord forbede ſuffre ſoueraign lorde ſlayne enoynted god therwith toke ſpere cup water whan good dyſtaunce hoſte saul cryed loude voyce abuer whiche thanne marſhall armye saul aunſwered ſayde arte thou thus dyſeaſeſt kynge whiche nowe reſte dauid ſayd abner thou thy company worthy deathe haue ſoo neglygentely watched prynce ſpeare cup water ſtode beddes hede suerlye ye dede men whanne ſhall knowe ſhewed ſpeare cuppe water whiche saul perceyuynge hearynge voyce dauid cried vnto hym ſayinge voyce deere ſonne dauid vncurteyſely purſue hym notwithſtandynge doth good euyll wordes abbreuiate mater paſſe ouer ¶ noble hiſtorie ſemblable miſtories hāgingis either wroughgt areſſe conningly paynted wyll moche better beſeme houſes noble men concubine voluptuous pleaſures ſame da uid salamon ſonne frequentely expreſſed hangynges houſes counterpoyntes vertue holyneſſe one wiſe experimentes nowe wyll paſſe ouer hyſtoryes whiche ſtraunge therfore ſuppoſe pleſaunte reder ¶ xerxes beinge kinge perſia gret cite babylō rebelled againſt louyng ſer uaunte ſuche ſtrength kynge power ſubdue perceyning gentilman one counſayle kynge xerxes named zopirus man notable wyſedome vnwyttynge peſonne dyd cutte owne eares noſe pryuely departed towarde babylon beynge knowen citie demaunded hadde ſo dyffigured unto aunſwered apparaunt token heuyneſſe moche hadde gyuen xerxes counſayle aduyſe reconſyled vnto theyr citie beinge meued ire dyſpleaſure towarde hym mooſte cruell wyſe cauſed hym ſoo ſhamefully mutulate addynge vnto reprochefull wordes agaynſte xerxes babylonian beholdinge miſerable aſtate token whiche ſemed approued wordes true moche pitied well greate wyſedome knewe occaſiō whiche ſuppoſed ſhulde incenſe hym ſhortly auenged made theyr chiefe capytayne commytted hooly hym gouernance defence citie whiche hapned euery thinge accordynge expectacion vppon ſhortely gaue notice kynge affayres exploitures finally ſoo endeuoured hym ſelfe wyſedome accorded kynge citie without loſſe damage eyther wherfore tyme ſayd kynge xerxes cuttynge odly great pomegarnate beholdynge fayre full kernel ſayde preſence counſayle leuer haue ſuche one frende zopirus thanne many babylon kernel pomegarnate alſo rather wolde zopirus reſtored agayne noſe eares haue hundred ſuche city babylon reporte wryters incomparably greatteſte fayreſt citie worlde ¶ parthiens ciuyle dyſcorde among ſelfes draue arthabanus kynge realme elected amōg theym one cinnamus theyr kynge iazate kynge adiabenes vnto whome cinnamus arthabanus fled ſente ambaſſade vnto parthiens exhortyng receyue agayne arthabanus made aunſwere ſens departynge arthabanus hole aſſent choſen cinnamus vnto done fealtie ſworne ſubiectes whiche othe mought laufully breake herynge cinnamus tyme kyng ouer wrate vnto arthabanus iaſate ſhuld come wold render realme parthia vnto arthabanus whā come cinnamus met adourned robe kynge approched arthabanus lightyng downe horſe ſayde wyſe syr whan peple expelled realme wold haue tranſlated vnto nother theyr inſtaunce deſyre toke whan perceyued theyr rancour aſwaged good wyll wolde haue agayne whiche theyr naturall ſouerayge lorde nothyng letted onely wolde nothinge contrary pleaſure good wyll drede occaſion ye may perceyue rēdre realme eftſones vnto therwith taking diademe owne hed dyd ſet immediatly vpon hed arthabanus ¶ fidelitie ferdynando kynge faythful tutor aragone forgotten brother henry kynge caſtill deceſſing made gouernour ſonne beinge infant fernando ſuche iuſtice ruled ordred realme parlement holden caſtille trayted hole conſent noble people name title kyngedome spaygne ſhulde gyuen vnto hym whiche honour fayning receyue thankefully dyd put vppon hym large wyde robe wherin ſecretely bare yonge prince neuewe ſo cam place ſayd purpoſe noble people aſſembled demaundynge euery man ſentence one voice gaue vnto kyngedome spayne toke robe lytell baby neuewe ſettynge hym ſhulder ſayde aloude vnto loye caſtilians behold kinge confirmynge harte auguſtus whan ſhewed many mē cite vnſittynge wordes thought ſufficient anſwere fre citie mē muſt haue tūges nedes liberte neuer perſon ſpake euyl hym worde countenance wors diſcon tented ¶ men wylle nat prayſe maner paciēce account foliſhenes remedy agaynſt impacience beholde ſide incommoditie cōmeth impaciēce howe man therwith abſtract fro reſon tourned monſtruous fygure cōferre ſtable countenāce pleaſant regarde p aciēt commoditie dothe enſue therof ſhall affirme ſimplicitie excellent wyſedome ¶ ouer beſte way aduenged ſo contemne iniurie rebuke lyue ſuche honeſtie doer ſhall laſte therof aſhamed atte leſte leſe fruite malyce ſay ſhall nat reioyce haue glorye thy hyndrance domage ¶ pacyence repulſe hynderance promotion ca xiii man hauynge gentyl courage lykewiſe nothinge noble man commodity happen aduancement good men maye nothynge excellente ye nothynge neceſſary aduaunce men eſtimation theyr goodnes two ſpeciall commodity come therof fyrſte therby prouoke many men apprehend vertue alſo whiche good redy aduanced gyue ſuche courage endeuour ſelfes al theyr power encreaſe opinion goodnes wher broughte aduauncement nedes muſte honour benefyte thoſe ſópromoted contrarye wyſe meu frome theyr infancye haue enſued vertue worne floryſſhynge tyme youthe paynefull ſtudy abandonynge al luſtes thynge whiche tyme pleaſaunte truſtynge thereby profytte publyke weale many whiche aptely diſpoſed ſtudy vertue hoped therby haue propre rewarde therof whiche commendation honour whiche beynge gyuen men lackynge vertue wyſedome ſhall occaſion yuell democritus ſayth douteth auctoritie good man doth publyſhe vertue lay hid yuell man miniſtreth boldneſſe lycence yuel drede couered ¶ surely repulſe vulgarly ſpeake puttynge backe frome promotion lyttell payne dyſcomforte maye withſtande leaſt remedied pacience whiche maye wyſe induced ¶ firſt conſideryng worlde pacience howe hit may induced neuer ſo conſtant tymes good men iuſtely rewarded none onely promoted ¶ cato called uticenſis whoſe wyſedome world wōdred whoſe grauitie wel ſenate peple rome kynges pryncis reuerenſed lokynge one conſules openly reiected wherwith frendes kynſemen toke lyttell diſcomforte cato hym ſelfe ſo lyttell regarded repulſe allwayes wente homely nexte day folowynge decked trymmed hym ſelfe freſhclye wonte whan ſhewed hym ſelfe ſo peple none walked one frendes markette place bare legged ſengle apparayle accuſtomed ¶ scipio called naſica hoole ſenate iuged beſte man citie auncyente howſe lyke wyſe put backe fro beinge conſule ¶ lelius lyke wiſe openly called wyſe man ſemblably refuſed dyuers hyſtories doo make mēcion abiecte whan well deſerued honour theyr inferyors merites promoted ¶ alſo mannes confeyence ſhal wel comforte hym whanne hath ſoo lyued ample without ſhe ſelfe may ¶ wyll lyttell tyme leaue noble philoſopher aryſtotelle reuerentely interprete place office tulli mooſte eloquentely playnely ſetteth vertue ſayinge alwaye valyaunte noble courage diſcerned two thynges ſpecyally wherof one dyſpyſynge thynges outewarde whan man perſwaded neyther meruayle thynge neyther wyſſhe deſyre thynge whiche honeſte ouer manne ſhulde bowe fortune trouble mynde nother thynge whan thou art mynde courage ſayde thou thanne practyſe thoſe thynges onely whiche greate moſte profytable alſo dyfficile full labour perylle well concernynge mannes lyfe many thynges therto perteynynge ¶ afterwarde ſame tulli ſaythe eſteme lyttel thoſe thynges vnto parte men ſemeth excellent alſo reaſon firme ſtable cō tempne ſygne noble valyaunt courage alſo tollerate thoſe thinges whiche doo ſeeme bytter greuous wherof many lyfe man fortune ſuch wyſe thou depart aſtate nature neyther worſhyp perteyninge vnto wyſe man betokeneth good courage alſo moche conſtaunce ¶ ſemeth magnanimitie good courage garmente uertue wher ſhe ſette oute moughte ſaye vttermooſte meane therby vertue amended made beauteous whiche ſelfe perfecte lyke wyſe ladye excellente beautye thoughe ſhe wayes ſayre yet ryche freſſhe garmente declareth aſtate cauſeth loked thereby naturall beautye better perceyued semblably doth magnanimitie ioyned vertue ſette wonderfullye furthe beholden mought ſay meruayled ſhall appere aboundauntly example enſuynge ¶ ageſylaus kyng lacedemonia begynnynge youthe perceyuynge greece great feare fame ſprade perſians comynge infinyte armye noble courage profred defende owne countrey alſo ſmall hoſt paſſe ſees aſia frome then eyther brynge victory perſians el ſure honorable peace whoſe courage lacedemones hyghely recomforted delyuered vnto hym x thouſande ſouldiours whiche hoſte went aſia vainquiſſhed perſians retourned ioyfully coū treye people ſaulfe perpetuall renoume alſo honour ſuertie greece ¶ antigonus kyng macedonia ſee one furthe vaynquiſſhed theyr enemyes ¶ suche noble courage great king alexander warres agaynſt darius ſene al people fightynge preaſe enemyes bare heeded ¶ wyll nat ſo vncurtaiſe leue vnremembred place notable magnanimitie kynge englande whiche hapned rede late olde cronycle ¶ edgar tyme saxōs realme ſubiection hadde ſubdewed kynges saxon made theym trybutaries tyme hym dyner ſhewed aynande king scottes hadde ſayd wondred howe ſhoulde happen kynges talle greatte perſonages wolde ſuffre ſelfes ſubduaed ſo lyttell body edgare edgare diſſembled anſwered nothing faynynge go huntyng toke hym example olde writer damage hath enſued obſtinacie conſyderyng euery hyſtorie full therof ſtyll haue dayly experience one thyng ſure obſtinacy ruleth reaſon lacketh place coūcel auaileth nat councell paſſed emperours deuiſed often time frendes haue reſygned auctoritie tyme senate ben wel furniſhed noble wife ꝑſonages ciuile warres betwene ceſar pompeie thought wolde ſurely haue reſtored publike weale priſtinate glorie nowe lette v ſee cauſe ambytion ſo pernicious publyke weale ¶ myn opinion two cauſes prin ambition il cipally fyrſte moche whyche courage appetite whan auctoritie ſuppoſe al thing lefull lyketh alſo reaſon preeminence wolde ſoo ſeperate man ſhuld cōtrolle warne enormyties finally wolde lyſte without contradiction wherof enſewe dyuers iniuries ſubuertion iuſtyce whiche meued thīges ageinſt ryght seing ſo time tulli whan almoſte euery man auctoritie de excellent lernyng romaine bryngyng vp child ſtudye morall philoſophye ſhall ſuppoſe tyme whan fewe men auctoritie experience ¶ ſecond cauſe condēneth ambicion conetyſe couetyſe treaſure therwith mainteyn oſtentation vaynglory whiche ambicious perſons doo call theyr honour wherby procured fynde vniuſte meanes auctoritie prouyde ſuche ſubſtaunce wherwith may nat onely ſatisfied beinge inſaciable accordynge owne appetite fully ſuffyſed wherfore philoſophers called stoici vſed ſentēce gret indigence lacke cometh nat pouertie great plentie hath moch ſhall nede moche ¶ certes ſuche ambycious perſones may well conſider magnificence pompe whiche couete nat ſo moch wondred auarice collection money vniuerſally hated wherfore darius plutarchꝰ apoth kyng perſia father xerxes whā cōmanded ſubſidie leuyed ſubiectes demanded chiefe men countreyes whether founde themſelfe greued anſwerynge merely good caſe commaunded one halfe efteſones reſtored leſte auarice ſhulde ſuſpected whiche acte ſtabyſſhed dignitie made perfecte ¶ ouer tulli ſaythe take ci iii thynge man one man encreaſe cōmoditie continence vertue whiche kepeth pleaſaunte appetite man vnder yoke reaſō ariſtotell makynge bothe one deſcribeth vnder name continēce ethi vii ſayinge continent moche knoweth coueitous deſyres yuell dothe abandone theym reaſon perſwadynge hym tyme take abſtynence refuſynge money poſſeſſions thynge ſemblable continence forbearyng vnlefull cō pany woman ¶ martius coreolanus noble yonge abſteynig rewardes coreolanꝰ man whiche lyneally deſcended ancus ſometyme kynge romaynes whan done many valyaunte actes achyeued ſondrye enterpryſes accordyng merites commended armye poſtumius conſull theyr vniuerſall aſſente rewarded ſuche honour apperteyned good warryour alſo one hū dred acre arable lande election ten priſoners ten horſis apparayled warres one hundred ox moche ſyluer moughte beare wolde take thynge one onely pryſoner whiche acquayntaunce one courſer whiche al wayes vſed batayle ¶ marcus curius rule paterne curius fortitude moderate liuing whā people called samnite warres romaynes founde hym ſyttyng houſe fire vpon homely fourme catyng meate dyſhe oftre bringing great ſome golde conſent people wondring pouertie courtaiſe langage deſyred hym take broughte therat ſmylyng ſaid thus vnto thē ye miniſters vaine ſuperfluous meſſage ſhewe samnite curius leuer haue domynyon ouer theym ryche hym ſelfe haue richeſſe golde ye accounte precious take agayne remembre ye neyther vaynquiſhe batayle corrupte money ¶ quintus tubero ſurnamed catelius tyme conſull people tubero greece called aetoli ſente hym theyr ambaſſadonrs great quantitie ſiluer veſſel curiously wrought grauen whan came hym founde table veſſel erthe whan ſawe exhorted ſhulde ſuppoſe contentation pouertie ſhulde theyr preſentes relyued ſaying commaunded depart ¶ epaminondas thebane beinge epaminō da tyme well vertue proweſſe moſte noble man grece arthaxerſes kynge perſya make hym frende ſent one ſeruauntes thebe greatte quantitie treaſoure whiche ſeruaunte knowynge maners darſte offre vnto hym whan came ſpeakynge yonge man famyliar epaminōdas gaue vnto great rewarde meue epaminondas receiue kinges preſent vneth herynge fyrſte wordes yonge man commaunded kynges ſeruaunte broughte vnto hym vnto whome hadde theſe wordes frende ſhewe kynge nedeth offre money haue thynge thebanes good purpoſe may haue theyr aſſiſtence rewarde purpoſe nought al treaſoure worlde hope obteyne ¶ whiche wordes ſpoken ſuche grauitie ſayde ſeruaunte beinge ferde deſyred epamynondas mought ſaulfly conuayed cite whiche graunted good wyll leaſte money taken away mought receyuynge therof haue ben ſuſpected ouer cauſed thebane whiche frende companyon reſtore meſſager money receyued ¶ semblable abſtinence pho phocion cion noble counſaylour athene vnto whome ambaſſadoure greatte kynge alexaunder broughte theyr mayſter hundred talentes gold whiche englyſhe money xii thouſand pounde herde theym ſpeke thynge demaunded onely kynge ſente ſo bounteous rewarde anſwered moche kynge alexander iuged hym good man iuſt ſuffre ye ſay de phocion ſeme ſame man king doth iuge cary golde agayne hym ¶ ſame phocion ambaſſadour antypater ſucceded greatte kinge alexander macedonia offred gyue great ſome money whiche phocion deſpyſynge ſayde wyſe sen antipater greatter alexander cauſe better doo nothynge perceiue ſhulde take thing whan oratour wolde haue hadde phocions ſonne haue taken money phocion anſwered ſonne wolde lyke vnto ſhuld haue nede neyther money none wolde vnlyke vnto hym dyſſo lute maners neyther antipaters gyſtes none others neuer ſo great ſhulde ſufficient ¶ theſe example doth appere good men dyd alwaye flee rewardes though mought haue ben lefully taken whiche neyther folyſhenes yet ruſticitie prudent conſideracion moche bothe wiſedome experyence knewe taketh rewarde thinge done lenger lybertye free man made bonde bycauſe hath taken erneſte true endeuour alſo takynge become yuel man though good receyue yuel purpoſe wretche deteſtable matter good ryghtwyſe ſelling good dede ought thankfully rewarde ¶ doubte ſoo euer contented preſente aſtate ſuppoſeth felycitie meane al exceſſe peryllous wyll alowe theſe ſentences thynke worthy remembraunce ſpecyally theym gouernours realme cytie men auctorytie haue theyr handes open money theyr howſes preſentes euer way de ſubuerted▪ wherfore caius pontyus prynce samnytes wont ſaye wold god fortune reſerued vnto time hadde borne whan whō vanquyſhed ¶ antfochus noble kynge aſia antiochꝰ citie epheſum behelde virgin beinge mynchen temple diana excellent beautie perceyuyng hym ſelfe rauyſhed loue maiden haſtily immediatly departed ſame temperate ſauing hath corrupt deſyres man lacketh ¶ alſo temperate man delyteth nothynge contrary reaſon contynent delyteth yet wyll lad agaynſt reaſon fynally declare wordes maye well call hym redoubleth treſpace ¶ semblable moderation wyſedome aulus gellius remembrethe plutarche aulꝰ gell philoſopher whiche mayſter trayane emperour hapned bondeman plutarch cōmitted ſomme greuous offence wherfore mayſter wylled ſhulde ſharpely punyſſhed commaundynge hym ſtryded naked cauſed ſeruantes prneſence beate hym ſlaue ſemid lerned beatyng cried plutarche maner reproche ſaide vnto hym howe agreeth thy doctrine preacheſt ſo moche paciēce al thy leſſons reproueſt wrath nowe contrary thyne owne teachynge thou arte inflamed wrathe clene frō pacience thou ſo moch prayſeſt unto plutarche without chaunge countenaunce aunſwered fourme thou embraydeſt cauſeles wrath impacience praye perceiueſt thou angry oute pacience ſuppoſe excepte moche deceyued thou ſeeſt nat ſtare myn eyen mouth imboſed coloure face chaunged deformitie perſone geſture wordes ſwyfte voyce louder modeſtie requyreth vnſtable geſture motion whyche ſignes euydent token wrathe impacience wherfore ſaid correctour ſens proue yet angry meane tyme whyle diſpute matter vntyll vtterly ceſſe preſumption obſtinacy loke thou ſtyl beate hym ¶ uerily myne opinion plutarch herin declared excellent wyſedome grauitie well exaumple pacience alſo ſubduyng ſtubborne courage obſtinate ſeruaunte whyche hyſtory ſhall expediēt gouernours haue remembrance whan accordyng lawes punyſſhe offendours ſelfes nat chaufed meued wrathe tulli ſayth like lawes whiche prouoked punyſhe nat 1 wrathe diſpleaſure equitie immediatly ſame auctour gyueth noble precepte concernyng moderation punyſhment ſaying correctynge wrath principally forboden punyſſheth whyle angry ſhall neuer kepe meane whyche betwene moche lyttell ¶ ſobrietie diete cap xxi verily nothinge doute part reders wark wyll take good parte al writen conſyderynge benefyte alſo ornament thoſe vertues haue ſpoken good reaſon congruence muſt ſhall planted contynewe knowe well chapiter enſueth ſhal vneth thankfully reſceiued fewe reders ne ſhall accoūted wor thy radde honourable perſon conſyderynge mattier therin conteyned ſo repugnant aduerſe pernicious cuſtome wherin longe tyme men haue eſtemed parte honour ſo moche wel knowe ſome ſhall people ſo moch openly called apollo turmentour ſayinge alſo goddis deuoured corn whiche libertie ſpeche perſwaded diſcontēted fro forth vſed ſuche frugalitie moderation diete contented ſeruid one meale thre diſſhes ſyxe mooſte whiche alſo moderate price yet therin vſed ſuch ſobrenes either hym ſelfe wold nat ſytte vntyll whiche dyned hym eatē good ſpace el ſatte whan dyd wolde aryſe great ſpace lefte eatynge purpoſe ſuppoſe ye dyd emperour wiſe neuer ſpot auarice vile courage certes two cauſes fyrſt knowing inconueniencis alway happen ingurgitations exceſſiue fedynges alſo lyke hym cō ¶ fyrſte ſacietie fulneſſe ingēdrid paynfull diſeaſes ſickneſſes ſquynces diſtillatiōs called reumes poſes hemorroydes galenꝰ de ſa • tuend lib v great bledynges crampes duſkeneſſe ſight tiſike required contēplation ſeryous ſtudy man hauing due concoction digeſtion expediente ſhall mornyng faſtyng lytel refection onely haue inuencion quycker iugement perfecter tonge redyar alſo reaſon freſher eare atten tife remembrance ſure generally al power wittis effectual better aſtate hath catē abundantly ſuppoſe cauſe auncient courtes recorde realme haue euer benne vſed kept none ſurely conſideration wonderfull excellent mought ſaye ſuperſtytiouſly obſerued reaſons ſo apparant nede nat reherſed ¶ pythagoras neuer ſene eate fyſhe fleſhe onely herbes fruites semblably dyd many exactely whiche laſte parte morall sapience begynnynge sapience politike ¶ nowe ye reders deſyre haue chyldren gouernours autoritie publike weale countrey ye brynge vp inſtructe ſuche fourme boke declared
